Nature of Deficient Time and Prayer Validity
Debating whether deficient time invalidates prayer performance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that deficiency in time is accidental (bil-'arad) to determine the validity of prayer performed in disliked times.

Core Idea
Time is never deficient; deficiency is accidental to performance due to resemblance to pagan worship.

This passage explores a key internal Hanafi debate: what makes a time 'deficient' and how does it affect the validity of prayer? The discussion centers on whether the deficiency is inherent in the time or accidental to the act. By analyzing the arguments of Fakhr al-Islam and Shams al-A'imma, you will learn the relied-upon position and its usul basis, particularly the concept of causality (sababiyya) of time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
The passage addresses whether prayer performed in a time considered deficient (e.g., sunrise, sunset) is valid. Two Hanafi authorities differ: Fakhr al-Islam rules validity, while Shams al-A'imma rules invalidity. The preferred view is the latter.
The deficiency is not in the time itself but in the performance.
2
Analyze the qiyas argument for validity
A qiyas is proposed: if most parts of the prayer occur in complete time, the whole is considered complete. This would validate prayer partially in deficient time. Note the objection: this would also validate if only a minority of parts are in complete time.
The illa is 'majority of parts being complete'.
3
Examine the counter-argument and its basis
Shams al-A'imma argues that the deficiency is not in time but in the performance due to resemblance to disbelievers' worship at sunrise/sunset. This is supported by the hadith that the sun rises and sets with the horn of Satan.
The deficiency is accidental (bil-'arad), not essential.
4
Understand the causality (sababiyya) of time
Time as a cause (sabab) is absolute and complete. Deficiency is only in the specific instance (e.g., time of redness). The causality is based on the absolute, not the specific. This explains why other acts of worship are valid in those times.
This usul principle resolves the dispute.
5
Extract the preferred ruling and its implication
The chosen view is that prayer in deficient time is invalid because one could avoid the deficiency by choosing a different time. The time itself is not deficient; the deficiency is in the choice to pray at a time resembling pagan worship.
Mufta bihi: Shams al-A'imma's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العصر لليوم الآخر (الأن سببه أي عصر الأمس أي (الجملة من الوقت (ناقص من وجه) دون وجه، فالواجب به لا يكون ناقصاً من كل وجه فلا يتأدى بالناقص من كل وجه، واعترض بلزوم صحته إذا وقع بعضه في الناقص، وبعضه في الكامل بأن شرع في الكامل وأتم في الناقص (فعدل) منه إلى أن الكل كامل اعتباراً بالغلبة فإن أكثر الأجزاء كاملة، وللأكثر حكم الكل (فالواجب به كامل من كل وجه ويرد عليه أنه يلزم أن يصح إذا أدى أكثر الأجزاء في «الكامل»، وأقل في «الناقص»، فإن المؤدى كامل باعتبار الغلبة كالسبب، فالأولى أن يقال إن سببية الجملة ليست إلا لأنها مشتملة على جزء ما من تلك الأجزاء، ولا نقص في هذا المطلق وإنما هو في خصوص مادة تحققه في وقت الإحمرار فورد) من أسلم في الناقص فلم يصل فيه لا يصح عصر القضاء (في ناقص غيره مع تعذر الإضافة في حقه إلى الكل) فإنه لم يكن أهلاً فيه، فالسبب ليس في حقه إلا الناقص، فينبغي أن يصح في ناقص غيره، ولا يبعد أن يقال إن سببية الناقص ليست باعتبار خصوصه بل لما هو مصداق للمطلق وهو كامل لا نقص فيه، إنما النقص في «الخصوص فقط، وإنما صح عصر اليوم مع أن سببه أي لمطلق كامل لأن الإيجاب لم يكن منه إلا بالأداء فيه، فقد وجب ناقصاً، وفيه أن وجوب وجوب القضاء بعينه وجوب وجوبه كذلك كان وجوب القضاء أيضاً ناقصاً فيتأدى في الناقص، فتأمل (فأجيب بمنع عدم الصحة فإنه لا رواية عن المتقدمين فيلزم (الصحة) هذا مختار الإمام فخر الإسلام، وقال شمس الأئمة: لا يصح، وهو المختار، وأشار إليه بقوله : (والحق، أن لا نقص في الوقت لذاته فإن الوقت وقت كسائر الأوقات، ولذا تصح فيه عبادات أخرى (وإنما لزم) النقص (الأداء) للصلاة (بالعرض) لوقوع التشبه بعبادة الكفار فإن الشمس تطلع وتغرب مع قرن الشيطان فيعبد فيه ( فيحمل ) هذا النقص في الأداء الشرفه وكماله وإلا فات، هذا الكمال (دون غيره أي غير الأداء، فإن فيه اختيار النقصان مع إمكان الاجتناب عنه، فلا يصح هذا، والله أعلم بحقيقة الحال.
The afternoon of the last day (now its cause, i.e., yesterday's afternoon, i.e., a portion of time (deficient in one aspect, not in another). So what is obligatory by it is not deficient in every aspect, so it is not performed by something deficient in every aspect. It was objected that it would be valid if some of it occurs in the deficient and some in the complete, such that one begins in the complete and completes in the deficient. So he turned to the view that the whole is complete considering the majority, for most parts are complete, and the majority has the ruling of the whole. So what is obligatory by it is complete in every aspect. It is replied that this would necessitate validity if one performs most parts in the complete and few in the deficient, for what is performed is complete by majority, like the cause. So it is better to say that the causality of the whole is only because it includes some part of those parts, and there is no deficiency in this absolute, but only in the specific substance of its realization at the time of redness. So it is reported that one who becomes Muslim in the deficient time and does not pray in it, his make-up prayer is not valid if performed in another deficient time, due to the impossibility of attributing it to the complete in his case, for he was not fit for it. So the cause for him is only the deficient, so it should be valid in another deficient time. It is not far to say that the causality of the deficient is not due to its specificity but because it is an instance of the absolute, which is complete with no deficiency; the deficiency is only in the specificity. And the afternoon prayer of today is valid even though its cause is an absolute complete, because the obligation was only from him by performing in it, so it became obligatory as deficient. In it, the obligation of the make-up is exactly like its obligation; thus the make-up obligation is also deficient, so it is performed in the deficient. So reflect. Then it was answered by denying the invalidity, for there is no narration from the predecessors, so validity is necessary. This is the choice of Imam Fakhr al-Islam. Shams al-A'imma said: It is not valid, and that is the chosen view, and he indicated it by saying: The truth is that there is no deficiency in the time itself, for time is like other times, and therefore other acts of worship are valid in it. The deficiency only attaches to the performance of the prayer accidentally, because of resembling the worship of disbelievers, for the sun rises and sets with the horn of Satan, so worship is performed therein. So this deficiency is borne in the performance, not otherwise, for in performance there is choice of deficiency despite possibility of avoiding it, so this is not valid. And Allah knows the reality.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is a dispute among Hanafi scholars regarding the validity of prayer performed in a time that is considered deficient (nāqis). The discussion revolves around the nature of time as a cause (sabab) for obligation. Some argue that if a prayer is performed partly in deficient time and partly in complete time, it may be valid due to the majority ruling. Others counter that the deficiency is not in the time itself but in the performance due to resemblance to pagan worship at sunrise/sunset. Imam Fakhr al-Islam opts for validity, while Shams al-A'imma rules invalidity, and the latter is chosen as the relied-upon view. The passage explains that time per se is complete; the deficiency is accidental to the act of prayer when performed at disliked times. The key principle is that the time's causality is based on its absolute nature, not specific instances.

Key Terms
وقت ناقص (waqt nāqis): A time that is deficient in one aspect but not another, specifically the time of sunrise/sunset or the 'asr of the previous day
سببية (sababiyya): The causality of time as a cause (sabab) making an act obligatory

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi position in the passage, why is a prayer performed in a deficient time (like sunrise) invalid?
A) The time itself is deficient and cannot serve as a cause for obligation
B) The performance resembles the worship of disbelievers, and one could avoid that deficiency
C) There is no narration from the predecessors about it
D) The majority of the prayer must be in complete time

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, time is never deficient; deficiency attaches accidentally to performance, and if avoidable, the act is invalid.

Distinguishing Wujub from Wujub al-Ada': The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Debate on separation of obligation from obligation to perform

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that wujub and wujub al-ada' are separate in both bodily and financial acts, and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument using the example of wudu and zakat.

Core Idea
Wujub and wujub al-ada' are distinct: one can be obligated without immediate performance.

This passage explores a key usul al-fiqh dispute: whether the obligation (wujub) of an act is identical to the obligation to perform it (wujub al-ada'). The Hanafi school holds they are separate in all types of obligations, while the Shafi'is distinguish between bodily and financial acts. Understanding this distinction has practical consequences for when an act must be made up, such as in the case of a woman who menstruates at the end of a prayer time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Recognize that the issue is whether wujub and wujub al-ada' are the same or different in bodily acts of worship like prayer and fasting.
This is a usul dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is.
2
Examine the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'is argue that in bodily acts, the obligation and the obligation to perform are identical, because the act itself is the performance. They use zakat as an example where separation exists only in financial duties.
Their evidence: no sin for delaying zakat before the year, and it falls by early payment.
3
Analyze the Hanafi counterexample
The Hanafis present wudu before its time: one may delay without sin, but performing it early causes the obligation to fall. This shows separation even in a bodily act.
This refutes the Shafi'i claim of non-separation in bodily acts.
4
Understand the rational proof
Sheikh Abu Mu'in argues that fasting has a reality (hāla) established in the dhimma, distinct from its performance. Performance is the externalization of that state, so wujub and wujub al-ada' are separate.
This is a conceptual proof based on the nature of obligation.
5
Apply to a practical case
The consequence: a woman who menstruates at the last moment of prayer time has no make-up according to Hanafis (because wujub al-ada' never arose), but would have make-up according to Shafi'is (because wujub existed).
This illustrates the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Issue: Obligation and Obligation of Performance. Obligation is not separate from obligation of performance in bodily acts according to the Shafi'is, unlike financial obligations like zakat. For zakat, according to them, before the year passes the obligation itself is due but not its performance, for it becomes obligatory after the year, evidenced by no sin for delaying from the time of owning the nisab until the year passes, and if one dies before, he is not held accountable, and its falling off by early payment with intention of the fard. So it is known that the obligation itself is due before and performance is not required. I say: wudu before the time is a counterexample, for there is no sin for delaying until the time, and it falls off by performance before the time. So they should separate in it too, and it is bodily. In the margin: it can be said that the speech is after the cause is realized, and here the cause for wudu is not realized, and it was not approved. He said that the intent is to refute the proof, which is necessary, for what was used as proof applies here as well: non-separation according to you. It can be established that falling off by performance with no sin in delay, and its reason is that the cause is realized at the moment of obligation, not at another time, for there is no room for saying obligation. Consider. And it can be answered that wudu drops obligation because the purpose (raising hadath) is achieved, unlike zakat where the purpose is performance which is an act of worship; if it were not obligatory before, it would not suffice. If you say: this is not valid according to Shafi'i because intention is a condition, so the purpose there is also worship. I say: the purpose is raising hadath, but according to him it is not realized without intention. This answer was refuted: for zakat, the purpose could be delivering wealth to the recipient from a specific source, the nisab; when it has reached, obligation falls. Perhaps this is an argument, for zakat is a pillar of religion and foundation of worship; the purpose of making it obligatory is to weary the obligated one by performing it in person. If it were not obligatory before the year, it would not suffice. The best in rebuttal is to say: zakat falls by early payment with intention of performing the fard; if one intends nafl, it does not fall. So it is known that it is obligatory and no sin for delay until the year, and before the year there is no sin, even if one fears death. So it is known that it is not required to be performed. Unlike wudu, for it is not performed with intention of fard; rather the obligation falls in the time due to removal of the cause of obligation, which is hadath. Its analogue is the falling of jihad by the death of disbelievers, or by other disbelievers killing them. Then know that the Shafi'i proof only indicates separation in financial acts, which is agreed upon, and non-separation in bodily does not follow from it. Sheikh Abu Mu'in strengthened their pillars: the bodily obligatory act is nothing but the act itself, like fasting, which is the performance itself. How can fasting be itself the specific abstention or other? The second is stubbornness and deception. On the first, it is either the act of the obligated or other. If other, then either it exists by his act, and his act is nothing but the abstention which is fasting, so the thing exists by its own requirement, or it does not exist by his act, then it is not voluntary for the servant to be obligated. If it is the act itself, and the act is the performance, so the obligation of fasting itself is the obligation of its performance: they do not separate, unlike financial obligations where wealth is something due in the dhimmah by Allah's command, and performance is an act therein, so separation is fine. This is explained at length. The answer: there is no doubt that fasting and prayer have a reality, which is the state that occurs in the person and representation, and performance is bringing that state into action. So performance is an act in it, as it is an act in wealth. Then we say: if by fasting one means the state that describes the servant, then it is identical to the act in the sense of the object, not in the sense of causing and performing. The Lawgiver has made it a burden on the obligated's dhimma, as He makes wealth on his dhimma. This is a kind of reality considered by the Lawgiver, and there is no demand at this placing. Then after that He demands from the servant to actualize that which is established in the dhimma externally. So establishing the state of fasting in the dhimma is itself the obligation, and its ruling is the validity of performance, and demanding the actualization of this established thing is the obligation of performance. Thus the difference is clear. And the meaning of thubut (establishment) in the dhimma is the Lawgiver's consideration that the obligated's dhimma is occupied with something that will be demanded to be actualized. As for the Hanafis, they said separation absolutely, i.e., separation of the obligation itself from the obligation of performance in both financial and bodily acts. So if a woman menstruates at the last moment (i.e., the time of the last part), she does not have to make up because the obligation of performance is not established. Unlike one who becomes pure at the last moment; she must make up because the obligation of performance is upon her. Know that this derivation was mentioned by the author that...
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage presents a major usul dispute: whether the obligation (wujub) of an act is identical to or distinct from the obligation to perform it (wujub al-ada). The Shafi'i position is that in bodily acts like prayer and fasting, wujub and wujub al-ada are inseparable; in financial acts like zakat, they are separable because the obligation itself exists before the year, while performance is required only after. The Hanafi position is that they are separate in all types. The passage provides evidence from both sides. The Hanafis argue using the example of wudu before its time: one may delay without sin but it falls by performance early, indicating separation. They also present a rational proof by Sheikh Abu Mu'in that fasting has a reality (ḥāla) established in the dhimma, distinct from its performance. The text gives a practical application: if a woman menstruates at the end of a prayer time, she owes no make-up (because performance obligation never arose), but if she becomes pure at the end, she must make up (because performance obligation arose). This illustrates the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
وجوب الأداء (wujub al-ada'): The obligation to actually perform an act that is already obligatory in the dhimma
الواجب البدني (al-wajib al-badani): An obligatory act of worship requiring bodily action, like prayer and fasting
الواجب المالي (al-wajib al-mali): An obligatory financial duty, like zakat, which is a liability in the dhimma

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in the passage, what is the consequence for a woman who menstruates at the very end of the prayer time?
A) She must make up the prayer because the obligation existed
B) She does not have to make up because the obligation of performance did not arise
C) She must make up only if she intended to pray
D) She must make up with a penalty (fidya)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi distinction between wujub and wujub al-ada' is essential for determining when a missed act must be made up.

The Basis of Qada: Nafs al-Wujub vs. Wujub al-Ada'
Debate on whether qada is built on original obligation or duty to perform.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between nafs al-wujub and wujub al-ada' and apply it to the case of the sleeper to defend the consensus on qada.

Core Idea
The sleeper's qada proves an obligation without immediate address — nafs al-wujub, not wujub al-ada'.

This lesson tackles a foundational usul dispute: what kind of obligation does the sleeper have? The consensus that the sleeper must make up prayer seems to imply an obligation existed during sleep, but the sleeper cannot be addressed. The Hanafi school resolves this by distinguishing between the original obligation (nafs al-wujub) and the obligation to perform (wujub al-ada'). We will trace the arguments, objections, and responses in this sophisticated debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core question
Is the obligation to make up (qada) built on the original obligation (nafs al-wujub) or the duty to perform (wujub al-ada')?
2
Examine the sleeper's case
Why does the sleeper pose a problem? He cannot be addressed during sleep, so wujub al-ada' is absent, yet qada is required by consensus.
3
Understand the two meanings of ada'
The text clarifies that 'ada'' can mean the obligatory act itself or the performance of the required act. This resolves confusion between qada and ada'.
The first meaning is nafs al-wujub vs. wujub al-ada'; the second meaning covers both.
4
Evaluate the objections
Some claim the sleeper is addressed via suspended address (ta'liqi). The response: immediate address is needed for wujub al-ada'. Also, Shaykh Abu Mu'in denies any prior obligation; refuted by consensus and hadith.
5
Analyze supporting evidence
The traveler's fast and the concept of substitution of cause for effect are discussed. Conclude that consensus supports nafs al-wujub.

مشغولة بحيث يكون الفعل مسقطاً للطلب الذي سيقع، ويستحق الحسنى التي تحصل عن الطلب ويأمن عن العقاب الذي يتوقع بالترك بعد الطلب، فهذا هو نفس الوجوب عبر بأي عبارة شئت وإن كان إقامته من غير هذا الاعتبار فأي شيء يقضي النائم والمسافر، وأي شيء ينوي المسافر حين أدائه وعمله بالعزيمة، هذا والعلم التام عند علام الغيوب وما قيل في التلويح أن الوجوب لازم لعقلية الحسن) لأن استحقاق الثواب لا يخلو عن نوع شغل الذمة، وعقلية الحسن حق كما هو مذهبنا فثبت الوجوب قبل ورود الخطاب فيرد عليه أنه يلزم ثبوته أي ثبوت الوجوب (بدون الشرع، ولم يقل به أحد منا
The discovery, and it is not in its text. It is understood from this that qada is built on wujub al-ada', but the following evidence indicates that it is built on nafs al-wujub. The apparent is this, because what is established in the dhimma, if it is not performed in the time, and there must be a branching, then its performance is obligatory outside its time. He said in the Hashiya: 'It is possible to establish the original speech: that by menstruation at the end [of the time], the causality shifted from the parts before it to [the point] where it ceased, so nafs al-wujub ceased, so she is not required to do qada; and by purity at the end, causality is established after it was not, so the dhimma becomes occupied and nafs al-wujub is established, even if wujub al-ada' is also with it.' And he indicated that this is not suitable as a justification for the branching, so it is better to make this from the branchings of the transfer of causality. It has occurred in the speech of Imam Fakhr al-Islam a branching: the non-accountability of one who dies before the end [of the time] is based on the transfer. This is similar. The author of Waqif al-Asrar said: 'You may drop the burden of the transfer of causality and say: qada is built on the original obligation, but on condition of its continuance. Here it did not continue due to the removal of eligibility at the time of demand, unlike the woman who becomes pure at the end, for the obligation is established with non-performance.' This slave does not understand this, for the removal of obligation after its establishment and the clearing of the dhimma after its occupation have no alternative from any aspect. How can the obligation be removed when its cause is established? So there must be recourse to the transfer of causality, for the causality of the cause has been removed and eligibility has been removed at the occurrence of another cause. So reflect. (And they argued by the obligation of qada for the one who sleeps the entire time, by consensus, which is a branch of obligation.) Because what the dhimma is not occupied with cannot be made up. It is either nafs al-wujub or wujub al-ada'. And there is agreement that he is not addressed for performance, i.e., the one who sleeps the entire time, due to the absence of address. Address is necessary, and address is [avoiding futility], for addressing one who cannot understand it is futile. If you say: Since the sleeper is not addressed and performance is not obligatory on him, qada should not be obligatory, because according to them qada is only obligatory by that which makes performance obligatory. I say: The word 'ada'' is used in two meanings: one is the very obligatory act, and its wajib either with the demand of performance – that is wujub al-ada' – or without demand, rather by its very being in the dhimma – that is nafs al-wujub – and its opposite is qada. This is what is meant in that issue. The second meaning is the performance of the required act, and it includes qada and ada'. That is meant here, so reflect. Then among the wonders is what occurred in some commentaries on the usul of Imam Fakhr al-Islam: that the sleeper is also demanded for prayer, but so that its effect appears in qada. For the demand may be to perform the required act, likewise it may be to perform its like, as in one who becomes eligible at the end of the time such that it does not accommodate except the amount of the takbir. In it, if it were complete, it would necessitate the establishment of wujub al-ada' due to the existence of address, so it would not be valid as evidence for the separation between the two obligations. Then it is itself also false, because the preventer of the attachment of address is the addressee's lack of understanding. For addressing the heedless is necessarily futile. The preventer is not the inability to perform, so that addressing could be valid with a supposed ability to appear in qada. So the truth is what we previously stated. Understand. And Shaykh Abu Mu'in objected, the gist of which: that the obligation on the sleeper after removing sleep is an independent obligation, it was not obligatory before by a legal proof. As for whether it is qada or ada', that is our custom. The ancient custom makes no distinction; it is said 'I performed the prayer as qada' and 'I performed it as ada' without difference. And the obligation of intending qada is denied; rather, he must intend what the Lawgiver made obligatory after the excuse is removed. Then there is no indication of the establishment of obligation on the sleeper. However, the people reported consensus on the fact that the sleeper's prayer after awakening is qada. And qada, although it is our terminology, what we have termed is a real meaning and was known from the Lawgiver. Consensus is on the establishment of this meaning in the sleeper's prayer after awakening. Also the hadith of qada speaks that the forgotten prayer and the sleep [prayer] are performed after awakening. So reflect. (It was said): We do not accept that addressing the sleeper necessitates futility. Futility would only arise if he were addressed with the act now, at the time of sleep. Rather, he is addressed with it after awakening. So the address is suspended (ta'liqi) and it is not impossible to attach to the sleeper, like the address attaching to the non-existent, for it is suspended and does not entail futility. The answer: The discussion is about the immediate (tanjizi) address, for it is necessary for the obligation of performance. The address to the non-existent is only valid as suspended. So likewise it is valid to attach to the sleeper as suspended, and that does not harm us. There is no difference in this suspended address between the child and the adult, unlike the immediate address. Accordingly, if a child wakes up as an adult, there is no qada on him due to lack of certainty of eligibility in the time, except precautionarily. And they also argued by the fasting of the traveler: if he performs it with the intention of obligation it is valid; if he does not perform it and dies before catching up with the days (qudda) from other days, he does not sin. So it is known that fasting was wajib on him and was not wujub al-ada'. It cannot be said that it is wujub al-ada' with a broadened obligation, because then the situation during travel and after it would be equal. For after settlement and catching the qudda, he should sin if he dies before catching the qudda, just as he sins with a broadened obligation after it, or he does not sin in both cases. Shaykh Ibn al-Humam answered these two proofs: that here the cause is substituted for the effect. So in the sleeper, qada is only obligatory due to his attaining the cause; and in the traveler, fasting is valid for that reason, not because the prayer and fast were obligatory on them. This is insufficient, for if substitution of cause means that the Lawgiver considers the dhimma occupied such that the act is a means of dropping the demand that will occur, and one deserves the good reward that comes from the demand, and is safe from the punishment that is expected by leaving after the demand, then this is exactly wujub, by whatever expression you wish. If it is substitution without this consideration, then what does the sleeper and the traveler make up? What does the traveler intend when he performs it and acts with resolution? And complete knowledge is with the Knower of the unseen. And what was said in al-Talwih: that wujub is a necessary concomitant of rational goodness, because deserving reward is not free of some type of occupation of the dhimma, and rational goodness is true according to our school, so wujub is established before the arrival of address. It is replied that this would necessitate the establishment of wujub without the Sharia, and none of us has said that.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute about the basis of qada (making up missed acts of worship) and whether it proves an original obligation (nafs al-wujub) distinct from the obligation to perform within the time (wujub al-ada'). The discussion focuses on the case of a person who sleeps through an entire prayer time. The author argues that the consensus on the obligation of qada for such a person demonstrates that a nafs al-wujub existed, because the sleeper was not addressed (mukhatab) during the time, so wujub al-ada' could not be present. The text explores two meanings of 'ada'' to resolve the apparent contradiction. It then addresses objections: someone might claim the sleeper is addressed via a suspended (ta'liqi) address, like addressing the non-existent. The author responds that the relevant address is immediate (tanjizi), which is necessary for wujub al-ada'. Another objection from Shaykh Abu Mu'in denies that the sleeper had any prior obligation; the author counters by citing consensus and hadith. The text also brings in the traveler's fast as an analogous proof, and Ibn al-Humam's response that it is a substitution of cause for effect, which the author finds insufficient. Finally, a critique from al-Talwih that wujub is a concomitant of rational goodness is dismissed because it would imply obligation without divine command. Throughout, the author maintains that the distinction between nafs al-wujub and wujub al-ada' is crucial and supported by evidence.

Key Terms
نفس الوجوب (nafs al-wujub): The original obligation that is established in the dhimma irrespective of the demand for immediate performance.
وجوب الأداء (wujub al-ada'): The obligation that includes the demand for performance within the specific time, requiring address (khiṭāb).
انتقال السببية (intiqāl al-sababiyya): The transfer of causality from one cause to another; here, the cause of obligation shifts from the original time to the excuse, affecting the status of obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi argument in this passage, why does the consensus on the sleeper's qada prove the existence of nafs al-wujub rather than wujub al-ada'?
A) Because the sleeper is addressed with an immediate command during sleep.
B) Because the sleeper is not addressed during sleep, so wujub al-ada' cannot exist, yet qada is obligatory, proving an obligation without immediate demand.
C) Because the sleeper is exempt from all obligations due to his state.
D) Because the traveler's fast is a stronger proof.

Key Takeaway
Qada is built on nafs al-wujub, which is established in the dhimma even without the capacity for immediate performance.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
15 min
Wujub vs. Wujub al-Ada': The Hanafi Distinction
Analyzing the separation of obligation from obligation of performance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between wujub (obligation without demand) and wujub al-ada' (obligation with demand), and apply this distinction to cases like the sleeper and traveler to derive rulings.

Core Idea
Wujub can exist without demand; wujub al-ada' includes demand.

This lesson unpacks a foundational Hanafi usul concept: the separation between obligation (wujub) and obligation of performance (wujub al-ada'). The passage argues that obligation can be established purely by cause (sabab) without any immediate demand, using the examples of a sleeping person who must make up prayer and a fasting traveler who is not sinful if he delays. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying rulings in cases where capacity or awareness is absent at the time of the original address.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core problem
The author begins by rejecting an argument that conflates wujub and wujub al-ada'. Recognize that the central issue is whether obligation necessarily entails a demand (talab) for immediate performance.
The key is that addressing a heedless person (like a sleeper) with a demand is nonsensical, proving that obligation can exist without demand.
2
Examine the sleeper case
Analyze why the sleeper's prayer after waking is considered qada (make-up). The obligation arises from the cause (the time of prayer) not from the address. The Hanafis argue that the sleeper was under an original obligation (wujub) but not under wujub al-ada' while asleep.
The author uses consensus (ijma) and the hadith of qada to support this. Note that the traveler case similarly shows obligation without demand.
3
Understand the deferred debt analogy
Consider a deferred debt or a lost garment held by someone unaware of the owner. These are established in the liability (dhimma) but not demanded immediately. This serves as a qiyas (analogy) for original wujub: obligation exists without a present demand.
Analogous reasoning (qiyas) is used: asl = deferred debt, far' = original obligation, illa = establishment in liability without demand.
4
Distinguish the two types of address
The author introduces the distinction between wad'i address (positional/causative) which establishes obligation (wujub), and taklifi address (obligatory) which demands performance (wujub al-ada'). The first is like 'The time of prayer is between these two times'; the second is like 'Perform the prayer'.
This distinction is the culmination: wujub is from wad'i, wujub al-ada' is from taklifi.
5
Respond to objections
Consider the objection by Ibn al-Humam and others that an act without demand cannot discharge obligation because intention of compliance requires knowledge of demand. The Hanafi response: wajib can be by cause, and compliance branches from knowledge of establishment, not knowledge of demand.
Also note the critique that the conceptual distinction does not prove real separation, but the primary evidence remains the sleeper's case.

تعليقي لا يلزم منه اللغو والجواب أن الكلام في الخطاب تنجيزاً فإنه لا بد لوجوب الأداء منه (والخطاب للمعدوم إنما يصح تعليقاً) فكذا يصح أن يتعلق بالنائم تعليقاً ولا يضرنا (ولا فرق في هذا الخطاب التعليقي بين الصبي والبالغ بخلاف الأول التنجيزي (فعلى هذا لو انتبه الصبي بالغاً لا قضاء عليه لعدم التيقن بالأهلية في الوقت (إلا احتياطاً) واستدلوا أيضاً بصوم المسافر، فإنه إن أدى بنية الفرض يصح، ولو لم يؤدّ ومات قبل درك العدة من أيام أخر لا يأثم، فعلم أن كان الصوم واجباً عليه ولم يكن واجب الأداء، ولا يمكن أن يقال إنه واجب الأداء وجوباً موسعاً، ولهذا لا يأثم بالترك، لأنه لو كان كذلك لكان حال السفر وبعده متساويين، فإنه بعد الإقامة وإدراك العدة أيضاً، فينبغي أن يأثم إذا مات قبل إدراك العدة كما يأثم وجوب موسع بعدها أو لم يأثم في الحالين؛ وأجاب الشيخ ابن الهمام عن هذين الدليلين أن ها هنا إقامة السبب مقام المسبب، ففي النائم إنما يجب القضاء لإدراكه السبب وفي المسافر إنما يصح الصوم لذلك، لا لأنه كان الصلاة والصوم واجبين عليهما، وهذا غير واف، فإن إقامة السبب إن كانت عبارة عن اعتبار الشارع الذمة مشغولة بحيث يكون الفعل مسقطاً للطلب الذي سيقع، ويستحق الحسنى التي تحصل عن الطلب ويأمن عن العقاب الذي يتوقع بالترك بعد الطلب، فهذا هو نفس الوجوب عبر بأي عبارة شئت وإن كان إقامته من غير هذا الاعتبار فأي شيء يقضي النائم والمسافر، وأي شيء ينوي المسافر حين أدائه وعمله بالعزيمة، هذا والعلم التام عند علام الغيوب وما قيل في التلويح أن الوجوب لازم لعقلية الحسن) لأن استحقاق الثواب لا يخلو عن نوع شغل الذمة، وعقلية الحسن حق كما هو مذهبنا فثبت الوجوب قبل ورود الخطاب فيرد عليه أنه يلزم ثبوته أي ثبوت الوجوب (بدون الشرع، ولم يقل به أحد منا ، ٦٨ لا ، فواتح الرحموت شرح مسلم الثبوت/ الجزء الأول كيف وليس لنا أصل (خامس هذا وقد عرفت أن معظم أصحابنا قائلون بالحكم قبل الشرع، ولا يلزم منه أصالة أصل خامس فإن هذه الأصول كاشفة عن الشغل الذي كان من الشارع جبراً لكون الحسن عقلياً، وقد قالوا بمعرفة بعض الأحكام بالفعل أيضاً ثم اعلم أنهم صرحوا بأن لا طلب في أصل الوجوب، بل هو مجرد اعتبار من الشارع أن في ذمته جبراً للفعل) بأن فاعله يستحق الحسنى التي يستحقها بالأداء بعد الطلب، ويبعد عن الضرر الذي يتوقع، بالترك بعد الطلب، وأما وجوب الأداء ففيه طلب وإن امتثل استحق الحسنى وإلا استحق العقاب (وأورد أن الفعل بلا طلب كيف يسقط الواجب وهو) أي الواجب (إنما يكون واجباً بالطلب) فقط، وقد قلتم إن لا طلب فلا وجوب فأي شيء يسقط بالفعل (و) أيضاً (قصد الامتثال إنما يكون بالعلم به أي بالطلب وإذ لا طلب فلا قصد للامتثال ، فلا يسقط الواجب بالفعل، فإذن الافتراق بين الوجوبين أصلاً، لا في المالي ولا البدني، بل إنما يحدث بالطلب يصح وجوب موسع إلى الأخير، وعنده يتضيق لا غير، وهو مختار الشيخ ابن الهمام (والجواب : أنا لا نسلم أن الواجب إنما يكون واجباً بالطلب) فقط (بل) قد يكون واجباً (بالسبب) أيضاً (والشيء قد يثبت) في الذمة ولا يطلب كالدين المؤجل والثوب المطار إلى إنسان لا يعرف مالكه فإنهما يثبتان في الذمة ولا يطلبان وهذا سند للمنع ، ولا تضر المناقشة فيه بأنه يجوز أن يكون هناك وجوب موسع إلى حلول الأجل، ومطالبة المالك كذا في «الحاشية»، وفيه إشارة إلى أنه لا يتم الاستدلال بهما، كما وقع من بعض المشايخ ولك أن تقول : لو كان الوجوب موسعاً إلى الأجل ومطالبة المالك لزم الإثم بالموت ،قبلهما، لأنه ترك الواجب في جميع وقته القدرة على الأداء، وفيه تأمل والامتثال يتفرع على العلم بثبوته لا على العلم بثبوت طلبه فلا يقتضي السقوط سبق الطلب هذا ظاهر جداً (أقول : فقه المقام أن لنا خطاب وضع بالسببية للوجوب كقوله عليه وعلى آله الصلاة والسلام : وقت الصلاة ما بين هذين الوقتين وخطاب تكليف بالاقتضاء فإذا كان الخطابان مختلفين (فيجب أن يكون الثابت بأحدهما غير الثابت بالآخر) وإلا اتحدا فثبوت الفعل حقاً مؤكداً على الذمة الأول) من وهو خطاب الوضع (وهو الأداء الوجوب نفسه وطلب إيقاعه في العين من الثاني وهو الخطاب التكليفي (وهو وجوب فعلم أن الوجوب شيء ووجوب الأداء شيء آخر) فينفصل أحدهما عن الآخر (و) علم (أن لا للب في الأول) أي نفس الوجوب (بل) في (الثاني) أي وجوب الأداء (وإلا) فيكون المفهوم من خطاب الوضع الطلب دون خطاب التكليف فانقلب التكليف وضعاً ولزم قلب الوضع فتدبر) وأنت لا يذهب عليك أنه لو تم فإنما يدل على مغايرتهما في المفهوم لا على انفصال نفس الوجوب عن وجوب الأداء في الواقع والمطلوب هذا دون ذاك، قال مشيد أركان الأصول والفروع واقف الأسرار أبونا قدس سره أنه غير تام إذ يجوز أن يكون مفهوم خطاب الوضع طلب الإيقاع عند وجوب السبب لا غير، فهو يفيد الطلب ولا نسلم المغايرة الذاتية بينهما، فحينئذ لا بد أن يرجع إلى الدليل السابق بأنه لو كان مشتملاً على الطلب يلزم في النائم اللغو، فإنه تعلق به خطاب الوضع هذا، وتأمل فيه، فإن فيه أخذ بعض مقدمات دليل في دليل آخر مع
From it: the second discourse on rulings except the amount of tahrimah. In it: if it were complete, it would necessitate the establishment of the obligation of performance due to the existence of address, so it is not suitable as evidence for the separation between the two obligations. Then it is itself invalid, because the preventer of the attachment of address is the lack of understanding of the addressee, for addressing the heedless is necessarily invalid; and the preventer was not the inability to perform, so that address could be directed with an imagined ability to show its effect in qada. So the truth is what we have previously presented to you, so understand. And Shaykh Abu Mu'in raised [an objection] the gist of which: the obligatory upon the sleeper after sleep ends is an independent obligation, it was not obligatory before by a legal proof. As for it being qada or ada, it is our convention, and the old convention is not different; one says 'I performed qada of prayer' and 'I performed ada' without difference. As for the obligation of intention for qada, it is denied; rather, he must intend what the Lawgiver obligated after the removal of the excuse, thus there is no indication of the establishment of obligation upon the sleeper. However, the people transmitted consensus on the sleeper's prayer after awakening being qada, and qada, even if it is a term of ours, but we have conventionalized it as a meaning derived and understood from the Lawgiver, and consensus on the establishment of this meaning for the sleeper's prayer after awakening. Also the hadith of qada speaks that the forgotten sleep prayer performed after awakening is qada, so reflect. (It was said): we do not concede that addressing the sleeper necessitates nonsense; nonsense would only be necessary if he were addressed with the act at the time of sleep, but he is addressed with it after awakening, so the address is conditional, and its attachment to the sleeper is not impossible, like the address related to the non-existent, for it is conditional and nonsense does not follow. The answer: the discussion is about immediate (tanjizi) address, for it is necessary for obligation of performance, and address to the non-existent is only valid conditionally, so similarly it is valid to attach to the sleeper conditionally, and it does not harm us. (And there is no difference in this conditional address between the minor and the adult, unlike the first immediate address). (So based on this, if a minor wakes up as an adult, there is no qada upon him due to lack of certainty of capacity at the time, except as precaution.) And they also argued by the fast of the traveler: if he performs it with the intention of obligation, it is valid; and if he does not perform it and dies before catching up with other days, he is not sinful. Thus it is known that fasting was obligatory upon him but was not obligatory of performance. And it cannot be said that it is obligatory of performance as an expanded obligation, for if it were so, the situation during travel and after it would be equal, for after establishing residence and catching up with the count, he should be sinful if he dies before catching up, just as he would be sinful under an expanded obligation after that, or he would not be sinful in both cases. And Shaykh Ibn al-Humam answered these two proofs: here the cause is placed in the position of the effect. So in the sleeper, qada is required due to his attaining the cause; in the traveler, the fast is valid due to that, not because prayer and fast were obligatory upon them. But this is insufficient: if placing the cause means that the Lawgiver considers the liability occupied such that the act drops the demand that will occur, and he deserves the reward that results from the demand, and is safe from the punishment expected from abandoning after the demand, then this is exactly the obligation, whichever expression you use. But if it is placing without this consideration, then what does the sleeper and traveler perform as qada, and what does the traveler intend when performing and acting with the resolution? This, and complete knowledge is with the Knower of the Unseen. And what was said in al-Talwih that obligation is necessary due to the intellectuality of goodness, because deserving reward is not free from a kind of occupancy of the liability, and the intellectuality of goodness is true according to our school, so obligation is established before the arrival of address. It is objected that it necessitates its establishment, i.e., the establishment of obligation, without the Shar', and none of us said that. 68 No, Fawatih al-Rahmut Sharh Musallam al-Thubut/Part One. How can it be, and we have no fifth principle? This, and you have known that most of our companions say about ruling before the Shar', and from it does not follow an original fifth principle, for these principles reveal the occupancy that was from the Lawgiver as compensation for the intellectuality of goodness. And they said about knowing some rulings by action as well. Then know that they explicitly stated that there is no demand in the original obligation (asl al-wujub), rather it is merely a consideration from the Lawgiver that in his liability he has a compensation for the act, that its doer deserves the reward that he deserves by performing after demand, and is removed from the harm expected from abandoning after demand. As for the obligation of performance, it contains demand; if he complies he deserves reward, otherwise he deserves punishment. (And it was objected: how does an act without demand drop the wajib? The wajib is only wajib by demand, and you have said there is no demand, so there is no obligation, so what drops by the act? Also, the intention of compliance is only by knowledge of it, i.e., of the demand, and since there is no demand, there is no intention of compliance, so the wajib is not dropped by the act. Thus the separation between the two obligations is original, not in financial nor bodily matters; rather, it only arises with demand, making possible an expanded obligation until the end, and at that point it narrows, nothing else. This is the choice of Shaykh Ibn al-Humam. (The answer: we do not concede that the wajib is only wajib by demand; rather, it may be wajib by cause as well. And a thing may be established in the liability and not demanded, like a deferred debt and the lost garment given to a person who does not know its owner, for they are established in the liability but not demanded. This is a support for denial, and the objection that it could be an expanded obligation until the time of payment or the owner's demand does not harm it. Thus in al-Hashiya, there is an indication that the inference using them is not complete, as occurred from some shaykhs. And you may say: if it were an expanded obligation until the time and the owner's demand, then death before them would necessitate sin, because he abandoned the wajib throughout its time with ability to perform. But there is consideration. And compliance branches from knowledge of its establishment, not from knowledge of the demand, so dropping does not require prior demand. This is very apparent. (I say: the fiqh of the situation is that we have an address of وضع (wad') by causality for obligation, like his saying (upon him and his family peace): 'The time of prayer is between these two times'; and an address of تكليف (taklif) by demand. So if the two addresses are different, then what is established by each must be different from the other, otherwise they would unite. So the establishment of the act as an affirmed right upon the liability (dhimma) is from the first, i.e., the address of وضع (wad'), which is the obligation itself; and the demand to perform it in the specific moment is from the second, i.e., the address of تكليف (taklif), which is the obligation of performance. Thus it is known that wujub is something and wujub al-ada' is another thing, so they separate from each other. And it is known that there is no demand (talab) in the first, i.e., wujub itself, but in the second, i.e., wujub al-ada'. Otherwise, the understanding from the address of وضع would be demand without the address of تكليف, so التكليف would become وضع and the reverse of وضع would occur, so reflect.) And it does not elude you that if it were complete, it only indicates their difference in concept, not the separation of wujub itself from wujub al-ada' in reality, and the required is this, not that. The one who strengthened the pillars of usul and furu' and the knower of secrets, our father (may his secret be sanctified) said: it is incomplete, for it is possible that the concept of the address of وضع is the demand to perform at the time of the cause, nothing else; so it conveys demand, and we do not concede essential difference between them. Therefore, one must return to the previous evidence that if it contained demand, it would necessitate nonsense in the sleeper, for the address of وضع attaches to the sleeper. Reflect on this, for it contains taking some premises of a proof in another proof.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a detailed conceptual analysis of the distinction between wujub (obligation) and wujub al-ada' (obligation of performance) within Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by critiquing an argument that would conflate the two, pointing out that addressing a sleeper with an immediate demand would be nonsensical (laghw) because the sleeper cannot understand. Instead, the obligation on the sleeper after awakening is a new obligation (wajib mustaqill) established by cause (sabab), not by direct address. The author discusses objections from Abu Mu'in, who argues that the term 'qada' is merely conventional and does not indicate a prior obligation. The author responds that consensus (ijma) and hadith confirm that the sleeper's prayer performed after awakening is qada, which implies a prior obligation. The analogy of the traveler's fast is then examined: a traveler can validly fast with the intention of obligation, but if he does not fast and dies before making up, he is not sinful. This shows that the fast was wajib but not wajib al-ada'—it was an obligation attached to a cause (the month of Ramadan) but with a capacity to perform later. Ibn al-Humam counters that this is merely placing the cause in the position of the effect (iqamat al-sabab maqam al-musabbab), but the author argues that this is insufficient because it essentially equates to obligation itself. The passage then discusses whether obligation exists before the Shar'? A key distinction is made: original obligation (asl al-wujub) does not contain a demand (talab); it is a legal consideration that the liability is occupied, making the doer deserve reward and be safe from punishment. In contrast, wujub al-ada' contains a demand. The author defends this by analogy: a deferred debt or a lost garment held by someone who does not know the owner are established in the liability but not demanded. Finally, the author distinguishes between two types of address: wad'i (positional) address that establishes obligation by cause, and taklifi (obligatory) address that demands performance. The first establishes wujub, the second wujub al-ada'. A critical note from a later scholar (probably the author's father) cautions that this conceptual distinction does not prove a real separation, and the primary evidence remains the impossibility of addressing the sleeper with a demand. The discussion reflects the Hanafi school's sophisticated approach to the nature of legal obligation, emphasizing that not all obligations involve an immediate demand.

Key Terms
الوجوب (al-wujub): أصل الوجوب: ثبوت الفعل حقاً مؤكداً على الذمة من غير طلب (original obligation: establishment of an act as an affirmed right upon the liability without demand)
وجوب الأداء (wujub al-ada'): طلب إيقاع الفعل في العين مع خطاب التكليف (demand to perform the act in the specific moment with the address of taklif)
الطلب (al-talab): الاقتضاء المباشر من الشارع بالفعل (direct demand from the Lawgiver for the act)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best illustrates the Hanafi distinction between wujub and wujub al-ada'?
A) A person who intentionally skips prayer must make it up; this is wujub al-ada'.
B) A person who sleeps through Fajr must make it up; the obligation (wujub) existed by the cause of time, but the demand (wujub al-ada') arose only upon waking.
C) The obligation to pray is always wujub al-ada' because Allah's command is eternal.
D) There is no practical difference between wujub and wujub al-ada'.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, obligation (wujub) can be established by cause (sabab) without any demand, while obligation of performance (wujub al-ada') necessarily includes a demand.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
12 min
The Hanafi Distinction Between Wujub and Wujub al-Ada
Arguing that obligation can exist without command, distinguishing it from performance obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafis distinguish between obligation (wujub) and obligation of performance (wujub al-ada) and apply the distinction to analyze the nature of legal obligation using khitab wad' and khitab taklif.

Core Idea
Obligation can exist without a demand; the duty is in the dhimma, while the call to act is a separate layer.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut addresses a subtle but foundational distinction in Hanafi usul: the difference between the essence of obligation (wujub) and the obligation of performance (wujub al-ada). Understanding this distinction is key to grasping how Hanafis view legal duties—some are established by cause alone, without an immediate command. The passage defends the Hanafi position against objections and clarifies the roles of the declaratory and binding addresses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim
Hanafis hold that wujub (obligation) does not contain a demand (talab); only wujub al-ada does. This is the central thesis.
2
Understand the objection
If there is no demand, how can an action fulfill the obligation? The objector argues that compliance requires knowledge of a demand.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Obligation can be by cause (sabab), not only by demand. Examples: deferred debt and lost property are obligations in the dhimma without being demanded. Compliance branches from knowledge of the obligation's existence, not from knowledge of a demand.
This is the key rebuttal.
4
Distinguish the two addresses
Khitab wad' (declaratory address) establishes obligation by cause; khitab taklif (binding address) demands performance. They are separate, so the obligation itself and the obligation of performance are distinct.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: an act performed before any command (e.g., before revelation) can fulfill an obligation if the obligation is established by rational good or cause, even without a revealed command.
This affects the theory of obligation before revelation.

في الذمة ولا يطلب كالدين المؤجل والثوب المطار إلى إنسان لا يعرف مالكه فإنهما يثبتان في الذمة ولا يطلبان وهذا سند للمنع ، ولا تضر المناقشة فيه بأنه يجوز أن يكون هناك وجوب موسع إلى حلول الأجل، ومطالبة المالك كذا في «الحاشية»، وفيه إشارة إلى أنه لا يتم الاستدلال بهما، كما وقع من بعض المشايخ ولك أن تقول : لو كان الوجوب موسعاً إلى الأجل ومطالبة المالك لزم الإثم بالموت ،قبلهما، لأنه ترك الواجب في جميع وقته القدرة على الأداء، وفيه تأمل والامتثال يتفرع على العلم بثبوته لا على العلم بثبوت طلبه فلا يقتضي السقوط سبق الطلب هذا ظاهر جداً (أقول : فقه المقام أن لنا خطاب وضع بالسببية للوجوب كقوله عليه وعلى آله الصلاة والسلام : وقت الصلاة ما بين هذين الوقتين وخطاب تكليف بالاقتضاء فإذا كان الخطابان مختلفين (فيجب أن يكون الثابت بأحدهما غير الثابت بالآخر) وإلا اتحدا فثبوت الفعل حقاً مؤكداً على الذمة الأول) من وهو خطاب الوضع (وهو الأداء الوجوب نفسه وطلب إيقاعه في العين من الثاني وهو الخطاب التكليفي (وهو وجوب فعلم أن الوجوب شيء ووجوب الأداء شيء آخر) فينفصل أحدهما عن الآخر (و) علم (أن لا للب في الأول) أي نفس الوجوب (بل) في (الثاني) أي وجوب الأداء (وإلا) فيكون المفهوم من خطاب الوضع الطلب دون خطاب التكليف فانقلب التكليف وضعاً ولزم قلب الوضع فتدبر) وأنت لا يذهب عليك أنه لو تم فإنما يدل على مغايرتهما في المفهوم لا على انفصال نفس الوجوب عن وجوب الأداء في الواقع والمطلوب هذا دون ذاك، قال مشيد أركان الأصول والفروع واقف الأسرار أبونا قدس سره أنه غير تام إذ يجوز أن يكون مفهوم خطاب الوضع طلب الإيقاع عند وجوب السبب لا غير، فهو يفيد الطلب ولا نسلم المغايرة الذاتية بينهما، فحينئذ لا بد أن يرجع إلى الدليل السابق بأنه لو كان مشتملاً على الطلب يلزم في النائم اللغو، فإنه تعلق به خطاب الوضع هذا، وتأمل فيه، فإن فيه أخذ بعض مقدمات دليل في دليل آخر مع
لا شناعة فيه واعلم أنه قد ثبت انفصال نفس الوجوب عن وجوب الأداء ببراهين لا تدحضها شبهة أصلاً، لكنهم ما اكتفوا بهذا بل ادعوا أن في غير الآخر نفس الوجوب فقط، وأما وجوب الأداء، فإنما يتحقق في الآخر، ويتعلق الخطاب فيه وهو وقت التضييق، وأورد عليه أنه لو كان الأمر كذلك لكان الطلب مع المطلوب، إذ حال التضييق، حال وجود الواجب، وقبله ليس وجوب الأداء، وهذا الإيراد لا اختصاص له بهذا المقام فإن في الصوم أيضاً يلزم ذلك، لأن اليوم وقت الصوم، وقبله ليل ولا طلب فيه للصوم والجواب أن الآن السابق زمان يسع الواجب فقط، ويتضيق عن غيره والآن السابق على اليوم المقارن للصوم يتوجه الخطاب بأن يصلي في وقت التضييق ويصوم في اليوم فلا فساد واستدلوا على ما ادعوا أن فيما قبل الآخران أدى سقط الفرض، فهناك وجوب البتة، وإن أخر فلا إثم، فليس هناك طلب، وإلاّ لأثم لمخالفة الأمر، فهناك وجوب من دون وجوب الأداء، وأما في الآخر فيأثم بالتأخير، ففيه توجه الخطاب، ولا يخفى ما فيه فإنه لا يدل إلا على انتفاء الطلب المضيق، فإنه إن كان طلب في الأول موسعاً إلى الآخر بحيث يتخير المكلف أن يؤدي في أي وقت شاء فلا يلزم الإثم بالتأخير ولا محذور، ولعله من ها هنا زعم المصنف أن المطلوب نفي الطلب الحتمي، لكن تنبو عنه كلماتهم في مواضع ثم إنه يلزم عليهم أن لا يتحقق امتثال أصلاً، ولا يكون الرسول عليه وآله الصلاة والسلام والصحابة رضوان الله عليهم ممتثلين للأوامر الإلهية، فإن الامتثال ايقاع المأمور به كما هو مأمور، وقد فرض أنه لم يتعلق أمر قبل الآخر، وفي الآخر لم يتعلق لمنع الأداء في الوقت السابق على الآخر عن التعلق فيه ولا يبعد أن يتكلف ويقال : إن عدم ثبوت الامتثال لأجل ثبوت ما هو أعلى منه، وهو ابتغاء رضا الله بالمبادرة إلى الفعل قبل طلبه غير قبيح، ثم أنه يلزم أن لا يتحقق التكليف المنجز في الصلاة إلا على أقل القليل من المكلفين الآتين بالفعل حال التضيق أو القاضين، ولعلهم يلتزمونه : هذا وقد وقع في هذه المسألة نوع إطناب، لأنه من مطارح الأذكياء، وزل فيها أقدام كثر من المهرة، والله تعالى ولي السداد.
No, how can we have a fifth principle? You have known that most of our companions are upholders of judgment before revelation, and it does not entail a fifth principle, for these principles reveal the obligation that was from the Lawgiver as a recompense because the good is rational. And they said that some rulings are known by action as well. Then know that they explicitly stated that there is no demand in the essence of obligation, rather it is mere consideration from the Lawgiver that there is in his liability a recompense for the action, because the doer deserves the good reward that he deserves by performance after demand, and is removed from the harm that is expected by omission after demand. As for the obligation of performance, there is a demand in it; if he complies, he deserves the good reward, otherwise he deserves punishment. An objection is raised: how can an action without demand fulfill the obligation, when the obligation is only obligatory by demand? You have said there is no demand, so there is no obligation, so what thing is fulfilled by the action? Also, the intention of compliance is only by knowledge of it, i.e., by the demand; when there is no demand, there is no intention of compliance, so the obligation is not fulfilled by the action. Thus the distinction between the two obligations is fundamental, neither in financial nor bodily matters; rather it only arises by demand, making a broad obligation valid until the end, and at that point it becomes narrow, no other. This is the choice of Shaykh Ibn al-Humam. The answer: we do not concede that the obligation is only obligatory by demand alone; rather it may be obligatory by cause as well. A thing may be established in the liability without being demanded, like a deferred debt and a lost garment thrown to a person whose owner he does not know; both are established in the liability without being demanded. This supports the denial. The discussion about it being permissible that there is a broad obligation until the term and the owner's claim, as mentioned in the Hashiya, does not harm; and it indicates that the argument by them is not complete, as some shaykhs have done. You may say: if the obligation were broad until the term and the owner's claim, it would necessitate sin upon death before them, because he abandoned the obligation in all its time while able to perform; there is consideration in it. Compliance branches from knowledge of its establishment, not from knowledge of the establishment of its demand; so the prior demand does not require the fulfillment. This is very apparent. I say: the fiqh of the situation is that we have a declaratory address with causality for the obligation, like his saying, peace be upon him: 'The time of prayer is between these two times,' and a binding address with requirement. When the two addresses differ, then what is established by one must be different from what is established by the other; otherwise they would be one. So the establishment of the action as an affirmed right on the liability comes from the first, which is the declaratory address, and that is the obligation itself; and the demand for its occurrence in the specific instance comes from the second, which is the binding address, and that is the obligation of performance. Thus it is known that obligation is one thing and obligation of performance is another; they separate from each other. And it is known that there is no [demand] in the first, i.e., the obligation itself, but in the second, i.e., the obligation of performance. Otherwise, the understood meaning from the declaratory address would be demand without the binding address, thus the binding would become declaratory and the declaratory would be inverted; reflect. You may not overlook that if it were complete, it would only indicate differentiation in concept, not the actual separation of the obligation itself from the obligation of performance; what is required is this not that. The strengthener of the pillars of usul and furu', the knower of secrets, our father, may his secret be sanctified, said that it is incomplete, because it is permissible that the understood meaning of the declaratory address is the demand for occurrence upon the cause of obligation, no other; it conveys demand, and we do not concede essential difference between them. Thus it is necessary to refer to the previous proof that if it included demand, it would entail futility for the sleeping person, for this declaratory address attaches to him. Reflect on it, for it takes some premises of a proof in another proof. There is no repugnance in it. Know that the separation of the obligation itself from the obligation of performance has been established by proofs that no doubt can refute. But they were not content with this; they claimed that in the non-last part there is only the obligation itself, while the obligation of performance is realized only in the last part, and the address attaches to it, which is the time of restriction. An objection was raised: if so, then the demand would be simultaneous with the demanded, since the time of restriction is the time of the existence of the wajib, and before it there is no obligation of performance. This objection is not specific to this situation; it also applies to fasting, because the day is the time of fasting, and before it is night, and there is no demand for fasting in it. The answer: the previous moment is a time that accommodates only the wajib, and is restricted from other than it; and the previous moment to the day coinciding with fasting, the address is directed that he should pray in the time of restriction and fast during the day, so there is no corruption. They argued for their claim that in what precedes the last, if he performs, the obligation falls, so there is definitely obligation; if he delays, there is no sin, so there is no demand; otherwise there would be sin for violating the command. Thus there is obligation without obligation of performance. As for the last, he sins by delaying, so there is direction of address. What it contains is not hidden; it only indicates the negation of restricted demand. For if there was a demand in the first, broad until the last, such that the responsible person may choose to perform at any time he wills, then there is no sin for delay and no problem. This is likely why the author claimed that what is sought is the negation of categorical demand, but their words in places fall short of it. Then it would entail that there is no compliance at all, and the Messenger and the Companions would not be compliant with the divine commands. For compliance is the occurrence of the commanded as it is commanded, and it was assumed that no command attached before the last, and in the last it did not attach because of preventing performance in the time before the last from attaching to it. It is not unlikely to burden and say: the non-establishment of compliance is due to the establishment of what is higher than it, which is seeking God's pleasure by hastening to the act before its command, which is not ugly. Then it would entail that actual binding obligation in prayer would not be realized except for the very few of the responsible persons who come with the act at the time of restriction or those who make it up. Perhaps they accept this. This matter has received excessive detail because it is a subject for the intelligent; many experts have slipped in it. And God is the possessor of success.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul argument about the nature of obligation (wujub) and its distinction from the obligation of performance (wujub al-ada). The author begins by affirming the Hanafi position that there can be obligation before divine command (hukm qabl al-shar'), based on rational good and evil. He then clarifies that the essence of obligation does not contain a demand (talab); it is merely the Lawgiver's consideration that a recompense is due. In contrast, the obligation of performance includes a demand, which carries consequences of reward or punishment. An objection is raised: if there is no demand in the essence of obligation, how can an action fulfill it? The author responds by citing examples of obligations that are established without a demand, such as a deferred debt (dayn mu'ajjal) and a lost garment (thawb mutarrah) whose owner is unknown. These are fixed in the liability but not demanded. He further distinguishes between the declaratory address (khitab wad') that establishes obligation by cause, and the binding address (khitab taklif) that demands performance. This distinction is crucial in Hanafi usul. The debate continues with counterarguments from opponents, especially regarding the time of restriction, and the author defends the Hanafi position by showing that the separation is proven by rational proofs. The passage ends with an acknowledgement of the difficulty of the issue.

Key Terms
الوجوب (al-wujub): The essential obligation established in the dhimma without necessarily containing a demand; it is a mere consideration by the Lawgiver.
وجوب الأداء (wujub al-ada): The obligation of performance that includes a demand (talab); it attaches to the act itself and requires immediate execution or by a specified time.
خطاب وضع (khitab wad'): A declaratory address that establishes a legal cause (sabab) for obligation without directly commanding an act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what distinguishes wujub from wujub al-ada?
A) Wujub is only for financial acts, while wujub al-ada is for bodily acts.
B) Wujub contains no demand, while wujub al-ada contains a demand.
C) Wujub is established only by revelation, while wujub al-ada is by reason.
D) Wujub is always broad, while wujub al-ada is always immediate.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, obligation (wujub) can exist without a demand, distinguishing it from the obligation of performance (wujub al-ada) which includes the demand to act.

Divisions of Wajib: Ada', Qada', and I'ada
Defining adā', qaḍā', i'āda with intra-Hanafi dispute on i'āda

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define adā', qaḍā', and i'āda according to the Hanafi school and explain the ruling on i'āda when a wajib component is omitted.

Core Idea
Repeating a prayer in its time is wajib if a wajib element was missed, because the liability remains occupied.

In this lesson, we dissect the threefold division of wajib: adā' (timely performance), qaḍā' (makeup), and i'āda (repetition within the time). The Hanafi school distinguishes i'āda from ordinary performance and rules that under certain conditions it is obligatory, not merely recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two primary divisions
The passage states that wajib is divided into two types: adā' and qaḍā'. Note that i'āda is introduced as a subtype of adā'.
Adā' means performing the wajib in its proper time; qaḍā' means performing it after the time.
2
Understand the definition of adā' and its alternative
The main definition: adā' is any performance within the time. An alternative (qīla) restricts adā' to the initial act (e.g., takbīr for Hanafis) done in the time, with the remainder outside.
This alternative affects cases like starting prayer before time ends but finishing after.
3
Define i'āda and identify its condition
I'āda is repeating the act within the same time due to a flaw (khalal) in the first performance that does not invalidate it, like omitting al-Fātiḥa in the Hanafi school.
The flaw must be serious enough to render the act makrūh taḥrīman but not bāṭil.
4
Analyze the dispute on the ruling of i'āda
Some say i'āda is mandūb because the obligation was already fulfilled. The more correct (aṣaḥḥ) Hanafi view is that it is wājib, since the liability remains for the omitted wajib element.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference; the relied-upon position is wājib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة [أقسام الواجب] الواجب قسمان : أداء وقضاء (الأداء : فعل الواجب في وقته المقدر له شرعاً) ودخل فيه المؤدي في الآخر من الوقت وغير الآخر، فيشمل الواجب بنفس الوجوب وواجب الأداء، الأداء غير ما سبق (وقيل) الأداء فعل ابتدائه كالتحريمة عند الحنفية وركعة عند الشافعية في وقته المقدر شرعاً ليدخل ما شرع في الوقت وأتم خارجه (ومنه) أي الأداء من (الإعادة، وهو الفعل فيه أي في وقته المقدر شرعاً :(ثانياً : لخلل واقع في الفعل الأول غير الفساد كترك الفاتحة على مذهبنا واختلف فيه قيل : مندوب لأن الصلاة الواجبة قد تمت، فلا جهة للوجوب مرة أخرى والأصح أنه (واجب) إذا كان الخلل أداءها مع كراهة تحريم، كترك الواجب، لأن الذمة بقيت مشغولة بهذا الواجب المتروك، فلا بد من أدائه وإذا لم يعرف
Issue: [Divisions of the Wajib] The wajib is of two types: ada' and qada'. (Ada': performing the wajib in its time as determined by the Shari'ah.) It includes whoever performs in the last part of the time or other than the last, so it encompasses the wajib by the essence of obligation and the wajib of performance; ada' is other than what preceded. (It was said) ada' is the act of its beginning, like the takbir at the start for Hanafis and one rak'ah for Shafi'is, in its time as determined by the Shari'ah, so that it includes what one begins in the time and completes outside it. (And from it) i.e., from ada' is (i'ada, which is the act in its time as determined by the Shari'ah) a second time, due to a flaw occurring in the first act that does not amount to invalidity, like leaving al-Fatiha in our madhhab. There is disagreement about it: it was said it is mandub, because the obligatory prayer has been completed, so there is no basis for obligation again; the more correct is that it is wajib when the flaw involves performing it with an act of prohibited dislikedness (karaha tahrimiyya), like leaving a wajib, because the liability remained occupied with this omitted wajib, so it must be performed. And if he does not know...
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the divisions of wajib (obligatory act). The author states that wajib is divided into adā' (performance within the prescribed time) and qaḍā' (makeup after the time). The definition of adā' is given as performing the wajib in its time as specified by Shari'ah, which includes performing it at any point within the time (whether early or late). An alternative definition from others (qīla) is that adā' is only the beginning act (like the takbīr for Hanafis or one rak'ah for Shafi'is) within the time, with the remainder completed outside; this would include cases where one starts the prayer in time but finishes after the time. Then the author mentions i'āda (repetition), which is performing the act again within the same time due to a flaw in the first performance that is not severe enough to invalidate it—e.g., omitting al-Fātiḥa in prayer according to the Hanafi school. There is a dispute: some say i'āda is mandūb (recommended) because the original obligation was fulfilled; the more correct (aṣaḥḥ) view in the Hanafi school is that it is wājib if the flaw involves leaving a wājib (like al-Fātiḥa) which renders the prayer makrūh taḥrīman, because the liability (dhimmah) remains occupied with that wājib that was omitted, so it must be performed. The text ends abruptly, but the ruling is clear.

Key Terms
الأداء (al-adā'): Performing the wajib in its prescribed time, whether at the beginning or end of that time.
القضاء (al-qaḍā'): Performing the wajib after its time has expired, as a makeup.
الإعادة (al-i'āda): Repeating the wajib in its prescribed time due to a flaw in the first performance that does not invalidate it, e.g., leaving a wajib element.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, performing a prayer again within its prescribed time due to omitting al-Fātiḥa (which is a wajib) is considered:
A) Mandub (recommended)
B) Wajib (obligatory)
C) Makruh (disliked)
D) Haram (forbidden)

Key Takeaway
I'āda (repeating an act within its time) is wajib in the Hanafi school if a wajib component was omitted, because the liability remains for that component.

The Hanafi Distinction between Wujub and Wujub al-Ada
Theoretical usul analysis of obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between general obligation (wujub) and obligation of performance (wujub al-ada), and apply this distinction to determine when the restrictive demand arises in time-bound acts of worship.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, general obligation exists throughout; the obligation to perform immediately only binds at the final restricted moment.

This lesson explores a foundational Hanafi usul principle: the separation of the general obligation to perform an act (wujub) from the specific obligation of performance that carries sin if delayed (wujub al-ada). The passage establishes this distinction through rational proofs and addresses objections that challenge its coherence. By understanding this principle, you will grasp how the Hanafi school conceptualizes the demand upon the responsible person at different stages of a time window.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two obligations
Identify the key terms: wujub (general obligation) and wujub al-ada (obligation of performance). Note that the Hanafi school separates them: wujub exists throughout the time, but wujub al-ada only in the final restricted portion.
This separation is not made by all schools; it is a hallmark of Hanafi usul.
2
Analyze the proof for the separation
Examine the rational proof: before the final time, delaying the act incurs no sin; sin only occurs in the final time. This indicates that the demand in the final time is restricted and qualitatively different from the broader demand earlier.
The proof relies on the absence of sin for delay before the final moment.
3
Examine the objection
Consider the objection: if the obligation of performance is only in the final time, then at the moment of restriction the demand would coincide with the performance, and before that there is no demand for performance, making prior compliance problematic.
The objector argues this leads to logical incoherence.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The response: the preceding time can accommodate the act, so compliance is possible even without a restrictive demand. The act performed early fulfills the general obligation, not the obligation of performance.
The contradiction is resolved by the fact that the broad demand suffices for validity.
5
Evaluate the consequences
Assess the author's critique of the objector's position: if only the final time has a demand, then earlier acts would not be compliance; even prophets would not be compliant. This shows the strength of the Hanafi position but also the need for careful reasoning.
The passage ends by noting the complexity of this issue.
