له يصح اتصافها بالوقوع والوجوه عنوانات فرضية من غير معنون أصلاً (و) قال (ثالثاً) سلمنا ذلك، لكن لا نسلم استحالة تصور المحال واقعاً، بل نقول (إن تصور العقل ماهية المحال متصفة بالوجود في الواقع (سواء اتصفت في الواقع وصدق العلم أم لا) وكذب ليس بمحال بعد كيف وتصور الكواذب لا يستحيل (أقول) في الجواب : إن أراد عدم استحالة التصور مع الغفلة عنها فلا يضر ولا كلام) لنا (مع الغفلة عن الاستحالة، بل المقصود أن المحال من حيث إنه معلوم الاستحالة لا يتصور وجوده إيقاعاً في الخارج) فإنه يرجع إلى تصوره موجوداً أو غير موجود ( فإن الكلام في الطلب الحقيقي) وهو لا يكون إلا بتصور الإيقاع، وأشار إلى هذا الدفع في الدليل بقيد الحيثية في المحال (و) قال (رابعاً إن في الأمر بالصلاة لم يتصورها الآمر متصفة بالوجود في الواقع وإلا انقلب علمه جهلاً (إذ لم توجد الصلاة ( بعد) تعالى الله عن ذلك علواً كبيراً، وحينئذ فقد صح الطلب من غير تصور وقوعه إيقاعاً في الخارج فانتقض مقدمة من دليلكم (أقول) في الجواب لا نسلم عدم تصورها إيقاعاً، بل (تصورها) الآمر على ما ستقع، لأن ماهيتها لا تنافي ثبوتها فلا استحالة في هو هنا ، ثم ، تصورها كذلك، وإن حرر النقض بالعاصي فلا يتوجه هذا الجواب إذ لم يتصور صلاته على ما ستقع، لأنه لا يقع منه شيء، بل الأولى أن يقول يتصور حقيقتها ويصفها بالإيقاع ثم يطلبها ولا يلزم من هذا وقوعها فإن العلم التصوري لا يقتضي وقوع معلومه، وهذا لا يتصور في
The third chapter on the subject of the ruling, which is the act. Issue: It is not permissible to oblige with what is impossible by essence, absolutely, in its essence, not relative to some powers but not others, such as combining two opposites, or that which is impossible by essence to emanate from the obligated person, even if it is possible relative to the power of Allah Almighty, like creating a substance from an originated power. The Ash'ariyya permitted obliging with the impossible by essence in the two mentioned ways, and they differed on its occurrence; some said it occurs, others said no. As for the customarily impossible, it is possible in essence and in relation to the obligated person's power, but customarily it does not emanate from the obligated person, like carrying a mountain. It is permissible to oblige with it according to us rationally, contrary to the Mu'tazila who do not permit it rationally. And it is not permissible according to us legally, due to His statement: 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity' (2:286). Consensus is established on the validity of imposing something that Allah knows will not occur, even if this non-occurrence is due to something else. In 'Sharh al-Sharh' there is even [an assertion] of its occurrence. For us, if obliging with the impossible were valid, then [that which is obliged] would be sought; the meaning of obligation and seeking depends on conceiving of its occurrence as sought. Otherwise, that thing would not be sought, but something else. And this is necessary. So it has become clear that if obliging with the impossible were permitted, it would be conceived as sought — i.e., in terms of occurrence. Conceiving the occurrence of the impossible, from the perspective that it is impossible and known to be impossible, is necessarily false in the external world. So the permissibility of obliging with the impossible is false. If you say: This is reasoning against common sense, because there is no impossibility when one says to the obligated: 'Bring about the combination of opposites or the impossible.' He said: This is regarding real obligation and real seeking. As for formal obligation, which is without real seeking, such as uttering the imperative form and saying 'Bring about the impossible' or 'You are bringing about the combination of opposites,' it is like saying 'The combination of opposites occurs'; indeed, the information about it is not correct in reality, even if the utterance is correct. Likewise here, the real seeking is not correct, even if uttering the imperative form is correct. We do not claim the impossibility of this utterance by this proof. Rather, it is said in the speech of the people of truth that its impossibility is due to another reason that indicates it; if the reason were complete, the impossibility of this utterance would be complete. The other reason is that uttering what does not intend its meaning is foolishness or jest, and that is impossible for Allah Almighty. And obliging with the impossible is a defect, impossible for Him Almighty. This reason includes the formal and the real, except that it is specific to Allah's obligation, so ponder. Some virtuous scholars have discussions on this path, and we have pointed to their refutation in summary. Now we detail in detail what he said: First: The conception of the existence of the impossible is not necessary for seeking and obligation. I say in response: That denial is stubbornness, for the meaning of seeking is nothing but demanding its attainment, and demanding a thing is only after conceiving it necessarily. And he said: Second: We grant that, but we say: Conception in some aspect suffices for seeking, and it is not impossible. I say in response: Knowledge of a thing by aspect is knowledge of the aspect truly and essentially, for there is no real knowledge except by the essence. So that which is sought is the aspect, because the sought is that which is demanded, and the demand attaches only to what is known. And it is assumed that it is other than it; how could it not be other? The impossible is only the possessor of the aspect, not the aspect. He pointed to the answer to these two objections in the proof by his saying: 'And seeking depends on conceiving its occurrence as sought; otherwise, that thing would not be sought, but something else. And this is necessary.' Then his comment is not sufficient, for we do not accept that knowledge of a thing by aspect is not knowledge of it at all. How? Knowledge is that by which a thing is distinguished from others, and distinction is obtained. Yes, it is weak knowledge where the essence is not perceived and is not fully distinguished in the mind. However, the condition of demand with this kind of perception is not granted. Yes, the proponents of form say that knowledge by aspect is real knowledge of it, not of its possessor, because what is essentially obtained is its form. But we, the group of truth, do not help them with the form; rather, knowledge with us is another manifest state. Even if we descend, we say according to the proponents of form that the possessor of the aspect, in knowledge of a thing by aspect, is known accidentally, but why is this accidental knowledge not sufficient for obligation? How, when by this knowledge it has gone out of being absolutely unknown, and is essentially attended to? And essential attention is sufficient certainly. So the correct answer is that conception as sought — i.e., actually — is necessary, and this kind of conception, whether by aspect or by essence, is not conceivable for the impossible, for it has no essence that can be described with occurrence. The aspects are hypothetical pointers without any referent. And he said: Third: We grant that, but we do not accept the impossibility of conceiving the impossible as occurring. Rather, we say: The intellect conceiving the essence of the impossible as qualified by existence in reality — whether it is qualified in reality and the knowledge is true or false — is not impossible. Why? Conception of falsehoods is not impossible. I say in response: If he means no impossibility of conception while being heedless of it, that does not harm, and we have no argument with heedlessness of impossibility. Rather, the intended meaning is that the impossible, from the perspective that it is known to be impossible, its existence as occurring in the external world is not conceivable, for it reverts to conceiving it as existent or non-existent. The discussion is about real seeking, which only occurs with the conception of occurrence. He pointed to this refutation in the proof by the restriction of 'from the perspective' regarding the impossible. And he said: Fourth: In the command to prayer, the commander did not conceive it as qualified by existence in reality, for then his knowledge would turn into ignorance, since prayer did not yet exist — exalted be Allah above that greatly. In that case, seeking occurred without conceiving its occurrence as occurring in the external world, so a premise of your proof is refuted. I say in response: We do not accept that he did not conceive it as occurring. Rather, he conceived it as it will occur, because its essence does not contradict its existence, so there is no impossibility in conceiving it that way. But if one raises the objection regarding the disobedient person, this answer is not directed, for he did not conceive his prayer as it will occur, because nothing will occur from him. Rather, the better answer is: He conceives its reality and describes it with occurrence, then seeks it, and this occurrence does not necessitate its occurrence. Indeed, conceptual knowledge does not necessitate the occurrence of its known object. And this is not conceivable in
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive discussion of the Hanafi ruling regarding the obligation of acts that are impossible by essence (mumtani' bi al-dhat). It begins by stating the rule clearly: it is absolutely impermissible to oblige an individual with something that is impossible in itself, such as combining two opposites, or something whose occurrence from the obligated person is impossible, even if it is possible with respect to Allah's power (e.g., creating a substance from originated power). The Ash'ariyya school is reported to permit such obligation, both in essence and in occurrence, though they differ on whether it actually occurs. Next, the passage distinguishes between the impossible by essence and the customarily impossible (mumtani' bi al-ada), such as carrying a mountain — possible in essence and within human power, but not normally performed. The Hanafis permit obligation of the customarily impossible rationally, opposing the Mu'tazila who deny it rationally, but they do not permit it legally based on the Quranic verse (2:286) and consensus. The text then provides a rational proof: if obliging with the impossible were valid, the obligated act would be sought. Seeking depends on conceiving the act's occurrence as sought. If the act is impossible, such conception is impossible because conceiving the occurrence of something known to be impossible is necessarily false. Therefore, the obligation cannot be valid. Then the passage addresses a potential objection: that there is no impossibility in uttering a command like 'bring about the impossible.' The author distinguishes between real obligation (taklif haqiqi) and formal obligation (taklif suri). In real obligation, actual seeking (talab) is involved, which requires genuine conception of the act's occurrence. Formal obligation is just uttering the imperative without real intent to seek; it is like stating a falsehood (e.g., 'the combination of opposites occurs'). The utterance is correct but the real seeking is not. The impossibility of formal obligation from Allah is due to another reason: it would be frivolous or defective, which is impossible for Allah. Then the text responds to four objections in detail, defending the necessity of true conception of occurrence for any valid obligation. The discussion affirms that the impossible, by virtue of its known impossibility, cannot be conceived as occurring in the external world, so real obligation is impossible. The Hanafi position is that even if the impossible is conceivable in some aspect, it is not sufficient for real obligation because the essence itself is not attainable. The passage thus upholds the Hanafi usul principle that obligation presupposes the possibility of compliance.

Key Terms
الممتنع بالذات (al-mumtani' bi al-dhat): That which is impossible in its essence, such as combining two opposites, or whose occurrence from the obligated person is impossible even if possible for Allah.
التكليف الحقيقي (al-taklif al-haqiqi): Real obligation that involves genuine seeking (talab) from the obligated, requiring the commanding authority to truly intend the act's occurrence.
التكليف الصوري (al-taklif al-suri): Formal obligation: uttering the imperative form without real intent to seek the act. It does not constitute real taklif.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is it invalid to oblige someone with an act that is impossible by essence?
A) Because the obligated person may not have the physical ability to perform it.
B) Because real obligation requires the commanding authority to conceive the act's occurrence, which is impossible for the impossible.
C) Because the Quran only permits obligations that are within human capacity in custom, not absolute possibility.
D) Because the Ash'ariyya school objects to such obligation.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, obligation of the impossible is void because real seeking requires the possibility of occurrence.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
advanced
12 min
Taklif al-Kuffar bil-Furu': The Hanafi Usul Dispute on Obligation of Disbelievers
Usul dispute on taklif of kuffar with furu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi positions on whether a disbeliever is obligated with furu', apply the Hanafi usul principle regarding shar'i conditions, and evaluate the proof from Imam Muhammad's statement.

Core Idea
A disbeliever is not obligated with acts of worship because faith is a condition for their validity.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut presents a classical usul dispute: are disbelievers obligated with the subsidiary rulings of Shari'ah? The dispute reveals deeper usul principles about the role of conditions (shurut) in obligation and the purpose of taklif. The Hanafi school is internally divided, with the Bukhari and Samarqand mashayikh holding that only belief is obligatory, while the Iraqi Hanafis and Shafi'is hold full obligation. This lesson unpacks the arguments, the derived proofs, and the thamarah al-khilaf in terms of punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Distinguish the Bukhari vs. Iraqi Hanafi views on obligation of furu': the Iraqis (and Shafi'is) hold that a disbeliever is obligated with both belief and performance of acts of worship; the Bukharis hold that only belief is obligatory, not performance.
The author sides with the Bukhari position, also held by the Samarqand mashayikh.
2
Analyze the usul premise
Understand the dispute over whether a missing shar'i condition (iman) negates obligation. The Shafi'is argue that lack of condition does not remove obligation; Hanafis argue that if a condition for validity is permanently absent, the obligation cannot be meaningful.
The author critiques the Shafi'i framing as leading to absurdities, e.g., a person in hadath would not be obligated with prayer.
3
Examine the proof from Imam Muhammad
Evaluate the statement of Imam Muhammad that a vow to fast made by a Muslim is nullified by apostasy; the Hanafi derivation is that kufr prevents valid performance of worship.
The proof is zanni in both thubut and dalala, and is subject to objections and responses as shown in the text.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is in Hereafter punishment: Bukhari Hanafis say the disbeliever is punished only for disbelief and sins, not for failing to perform acts of worship; Iraqi Hanafis and Shafi'is say he is punished for both.
This is the key consequence discussed at the end of the passage.

وليست المسألة محفوظة عن أبي حنيفة وأصحابه، وإنما المشايخ اللاحقون استنبطوها من الفروع الفقهية، فإنهم أخذوا من قول الإمام محمد فيمن نذر صوم شهر فارتد والعياذ بالله لم يلزمه بعد الإسلام، فعلم أن الكفر يبطل أداء العبادات، ورد بأن التزام القربة قربة فتبطله الردة فلم يجب، فإن قلت : إن الالتزام كان في الإسلام ويبطل بالردة كونه قربة لا نفس الالتزام فيبقى أثره وهو الوجوب، قلت: الالتزام لم يكن موجباً إلا لأنه قربة لا غير لا سيما على رأينا، فإن العلة صيانة ما سلم قولاً مر، فإذا بطل بالردة كونه قربة بطل سبب الوجوب بما هو سبب وللرد وجه آخر ذكره مطلع الأسرار الإلهية قدس سره أن الإسلام يجب ما قبله فلم يبق بعد الإسلام عليه شيء فتأمل فيه، وها هنا مسائل نقلها المصنف عن الشيخ سراج الدين أنها تدل على أن مذهبهم ذلك ، وهي كافر دخل مكة وأسلم ثم أحرم لا يلزمه دم، لأنه لا يجب عليه أن يدخل محرماً، ولو كان له عبد مسلم لا يلزمه صدقة الفطر عنه ، لأنها ليست بواجبة عليه، ولو حلف ثم أسلم وحنث فيه لا تلزمه الكفارة والكتابية المطلقة الرجعية تنقطع رجعتها بانقطاع الدم في الثالثة بعدم وجوب الغسل عليها وعدم لزوم الأحكام بخلاف المسلمة وقال في «الحاشية»: وفيه ما فيه، أما في الأولى فلأنه لا يلزم الدم، لأن الإسلام يجب جناية مجاوزة الميقات، وأما في الثانية فلأن المقصود أنه لا يجب أداؤها إذ لا فائدة فيه وأما في الثالثة فلأن الإسلام يجب محافظة الإيمان، وأما الرابعة فإنما تتأتى إذا فرض انقطاع الحيض لأقل من عشرة، قال مطلع الأسرار الإلهية لا وجه يظهر إلا عدم وجوب الغسل عليها ويمكن أن يقال: إن علة وجوب الطهارة عندنا تمكن أداء الصلاة ولما لم يكن الأداء منها ميسراً أصلاً لم يكن لوجوب الطهارة فائدة فلم يجب، فتأمل فيه للنافي أوّلاً لو صح تكليفهم بالفروع الصحت منه إذا أدى الموافقة الأمر، واللازم باطل اتفاقاً قلنا : منقوض بالجنب فإنه لو كانت الصلاة واجبة عليه لصحت منه واللازم باطل والحل أنها أي العبادات تصح مقارنات بالشرط الذي هو كما وجوب
Issue: The disbeliever is obligated with the subsidiary rulings according to the Shafi'is and our Iraqi mashayikh, contrary to the Hanafis of Bukhara, and it is said also to the Mu'tazila. And it is said he is obligated only with prohibitions. As for obligation with penalties and transactions, there is agreement between us and them through the contract of dhimma. The contract of dhimma only necessitates that penalties be executed upon them as they are executed upon us, and transactions be executed and annulled as our contracts are executed and annulled except what is excluded. It does not necessitate that they are obligated religiously such that they are held accountable in the Hereafter for committing the forbidden and engaging in invalid contracts. If that were established, they would demand a distinction between them and acts of worship, unless it is said that abstentions are valid without faith, unlike acts of worship. In al-Tahrir, that is, the non-obligation of the disbeliever is the madhhab of the mashayikh of Samarqand, while the rest of the mashayikh agree on obligation. In the books of the Shafi'is, the dispute is formulated thus: When the conditions for the obligation of an act are complete but its shar'i condition is lacking, is obligation valid? According to the Shafi'is, yes; according to the Hanafis, no. They say we discuss a specific part of it, which is the obligation of the disbeliever. Since this has no effect in our books and is also corrupt in itself, it is not befitting for anyone claiming Islam to utter contradiction between the lack of a shar'i condition and obligation, for it would entail that a person in hadath is not obligated with prayer, likewise a junub, and that no one is obligated with Hajj except after ihram, nor with prayer except after takbir tahrima, nor with fasting except after intention, nor is i'tikaf by vow obligated except after starting the fast. How could they attribute such a terrible statement to these great scholars? The author wanted to clarify the point of dispute and said: They only differed concerning that the subsidiary rulings in terms of performance (ada') are obligatory upon them like belief (i'tiqad) which is obligatory upon them, or that they are obligatory only in terms of belief. So the Iraqis among our mashayikh say the first (i.e., equality of performance with belief in obligation), like the Shafi'is who say so, so they are punished for leaving them both. The Bukharis among our mashayikh say the second, i.e., only belief; so they hold them to be punished for leaving belief, and for the subsidiary rulings not for leaving their performance. Therefore, it is clear that this is an independent issue, not a part of another issue. It is also clear to you that the benefit appears only in terms of punishment. So if we suppose agreement regarding the otherworldly accountability, as appears from the speech of some mashayikh, the disagreement remains not at all in any way, except verbally. Know that all agreed that the disbelievers who die upon disbelief are eternally in the Fire according to their intensity in disbelief, falling into levels: the hypocrites are in the lowest level of the Fire. However, they differed whether this severe punishment is solely for disbelief or also for sins. The Bukharis said the first, the Iraqis the second. Then, obligation with subsidiary rulings is only for polishing good character, perfecting faith, drawing near to Allah, and attaining ranks. The disbeliever is not suitable for any of this, so he is not suitable for obligation. So his example according to the Bukharis is like a sick person for whom medicine is not expected to take effect, so the doctor turns away from him. Allah's turning away is not an honor for them, but rather a complete humiliation. Thus the objection that disbelief does not warrant the alleviation of obligation is refuted. Understand. And this issue is not preserved from Abu Hanifa and his companions; rather, the later mashayikh derived it from juristic subsidiary rulings. They took from the statement of Imam Muhammad: whoever made a vow to fast a month then apostatized (may Allah protect us), it is not binding upon him after Islam. Thus they learned that disbelief invalidates the performance of acts of worship. It was responded that undertaking a good deed is a good deed, so apostasy nullifies it. This was not answered. If you say: the undertaking was in Islam and apostasy nullifies its being a good deed, not the undertaking itself, so its effect remains, i.e., obligation. I say: the undertaking was not obligatory except because it is a good deed, especially in our view, for the cause is safeguarding what is sound, as said. So when its being a good deed is nullified by apostasy, the cause of obligation is nullified in its capacity as cause. There is another aspect mentioned by Mutila' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyyah (may Allah sanctify his soul): Islam wipes out what came before it, so nothing remains upon him after Islam. So reflect on it. Here are issues that the author transmitted from Shaykh Siraj al-Din indicating that their madhhab is that: a disbeliever enters Mecca, then embraces Islam, then enters ihram; he is not required to pay a blood penalty (dam), because he is not obligated to enter ihram as a muhrim. If he owned a Muslim slave, he is not required to pay sadaqat al-fitr for him, because it is not obligatory upon him. If he swore, then embraced Islam, then broke his oath, no expiation is required of him. And a kitaabi wife who is given a revocable divorce, her revocability ends with the cessation of menstruation in the third time due to the non-obligation of ghusl upon her and the non-application of rulings, unlike a Muslim woman. He said in al-Hashiyah: There is something in it. As for the first, he is not required to pay the blood penalty because Islam wipes out the crime of passing the miqat. As for the second, because the intent is that it is not obligatory to perform it since there is no benefit in it. As for the third, because Islam preserves faith. As for the fourth, it occurs if we assume the cessation of menstruation in less than ten days. Mutila' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyyah said: No aspect appears except the non-obligation of ghusl upon her, and it can be said: the cause for the obligation of purification according to us is the ability to perform prayer. Since performance from her is not possible at all, there is no benefit in the obligation of purification, so it is not obligatory. Reflect on it. For the denier, first: if their obligation with subsidiary rulings were valid, it would be valid from them when they perform in accordance with the command. The consequent is invalid by agreement. We say: it is disproved by the junub: if prayer were obligatory upon him, it would be valid from him, and the consequent is invalid. The solution is that acts of worship are valid only when accompanied by the condition, which is like wajib.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage discusses the usul dispute regarding whether a disbeliever is obligated with the subsidiary rulings (furu') of Shari'ah, such as prayer, fasting, etc. The author begins by presenting the different positions: the Shafi'is and the Iraqi Hanafi mashayikh hold that disbelievers are fully obligated with these rulings, meaning they are commanded to perform them and will be punished for leaving them. The Hanafis of Bukhara (and some say the Mu'tazila) hold that they are only obligated with belief (i'tiqad) and not with performance (ada') of acts of worship, though they are still liable for prohibitions and transactions. The author notes that there is agreement that certain matters like criminal penalties and contracts apply to dhimmis through the contract of dhimma, but this does not entail religious obligation (taklif diyanatan) that results in accountability in the Hereafter. The key difference is that acts of worship require faith to be valid, while abstentions (like avoiding the forbidden) do not. The text then explains that the dispute is often framed in Shafi'i books as: when the conditions for obligation are present but a shar'i condition (like faith or purification) is missing, is obligation valid? The Shafi'is say yes, the Hanafis say no. The author critiques this framing, saying it would lead to absurdities like not obligating a person in hadath with prayer, etc. He insists that the correct framing is the specific one about the disbeliever. The disagreement is about whether the disbeliever is punished for not performing acts of worship in addition to disbelief. The Bukharis say punishment is only for disbelief, while the Iraqis say for both. The author then explains the rationale: obligation is for perfection and proximity to Allah, which the disbeliever is not suited for; thus it is like a doctor turning away from a patient whom medicine will not help. The passage then notes that this position is not directly from Abu Hanifa but derived from subsidiary rulings, like Imam Muhammad's statement that a vow to fast is nullified by apostasy. The author also presents counterexamples from Hanafi fiqh that seem to support the Iraqi view, such as a disbeliever entering Mecca and later becoming Muslim not being required to pay a blood penalty for ihram, etc. Finally, he addresses an objection: if the kafir were obligated, his actions would be valid if performed correctly. He responds using the analogy of a junub (person in need of ghusl): his prayer is not valid without purification, even if he is obligated to pray. Similarly, the kafir's actions require iman for validity.

Key Terms
تكليف (taklif): The imposition of a legal obligation upon a person
فروع (furu'): Subsidiary rulings, i.e., practical obligations like prayer, fasting, zakat, etc.
أداء (ada'): Performance of an act of worship at its prescribed time
اعتقاد (i'tiqad): Belief in the heart; the inner conviction
شرط شرعي (shart shar'i): A legal condition required for the validity of an act, e.g., wudu for prayer, iman for worship.
جزئي (juz'i): A specific part or instance, as opposed to a general principle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Bukhari Hanafis, what is the consequence for a disbeliever who dies without performing the pilgrimage?
A) He will be punished for not performing Hajj in addition to his disbelief.
B) He will not be punished for not performing Hajj because he was not obligated with its performance.
C) He will be forced to perform it in the Hereafter.
D) His disbelief is forgiven if he performs Hajj in his lifetime.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul distinction between conditions of obligation and conditions of performance leads to the view that the kafir is not obligated with acts of worship that require iman for validity.

Can Non-Existence Be the Object of a Command?
Analysis of the principle that non-existence cannot be directly commanded.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi argument that taklif attaches only to acts, identify the rational proof that will requires thing-ness, and apply this to prohibitions.

Core Idea
Non-existence cannot be commanded directly; only the act of refraining (kaff) is commanded in prohibitions.

This passage addresses a fundamental usul question: can a command relate to non-existence? The Hanafi school firmly holds that obligation (taklif) attaches only to acts (af‘al). Against the Mu‘tazila who claim that non-existence can be directly commanded, the text provides a rational proof based on the nature of divine will (mashiyyah). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly analysing prohibitions (nawāhi) and the role of human power (qudrah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Recognize that the Hanafis oppose the Mu'tazila on the object of command. The Mu'tazila claim that obligation can attach to non-existence (al-‘adam), while the Hanafis insist it attaches only to an act (fi‘l).
The dispute is about the mahkūm bih (the object of command).
2
Understand the Hanafi position on prohibitions
In prohibitions (nawāhi), the commanded thing is the act of refraining (kaff an-nafs). This kaff is a real, existent act of the self, not a mere absence of action.
Kaff is an act, not non-existence.
3
Analyse the rational proof
The proof: divine will (mashiyyah) requires thing-ness (shay’iyyah). Non-existence as such is pure nothing, so will cannot attach to it. Therefore, the command cannot be directly for non-existence.
This is a dalīl ‘aqlī (rational proof).
4
Trace the role of power (qudrah)
Non-existence itself is not within human power because it is eternal and pre-dates power. What is within power is the continuation of non-existence through the continuation of the means (kaff). Thus, power’s effect is continuation, not origination of non-existence.
This refutes the objection that non-existence cannot be an effect of power.
5
Apply to a concrete prohibition
Take the prohibition of drinking khamr. The commanded act is not 'do not have non-existence of drinking' but 'refrain from drinking' – an active withholding. This real act is what is rewarded, not the mere absence of consumption.
The commanded act is kaff, not ‘adam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
لا تكليف إلا بالفعل خلافاً لكثير من المعتزلة القائلين بتعلقه بالعدم أيضاً (وهو) أي الفعل في النهي كف النفس ولما كان النزاع يرجع إلى أن العدم هل يصلح لتعلق التكليف به أم لا، وكان مبناه أن العدم مقدور أم لا، أراد أن يبين هذا المعنى لتنكشف المسألة انكشافاً تاماً فقال (لا نزاع) لأحد في عدم الفعل بعدم المشيئة، فإن علة العدم عدم علة الوجود والمشيئة من علل الوجود، ولكن لا يصلح هذا العدم مناطاً للتكليف والثواب (بل) النزاع في عدم الفعل للمشيئة) المتعلقة به هل عدم في الواقع بهذه الصفة أم لا (وهو) أي هذا العدم (الذي يتحقق به الامتثال في النهي ويترتب عليه الثواب) لو تحقق ( فنحن نقول : لا تتعلق به أي العدم (المشيئة بالذات فليس العدم الناشيء عن المشيئة متحققاً في الواقع (لأنها) أي المشيئة (تقتضي الشيئية) وهو ظاهر (والعدم من حيث هو هو لا شيء محض فلا تتعلق المشيئة به فلا سبيل إليه) أي العدم (إلا) بتعلقها) أي المشيئة (بما هو وسيلة إليه، وهو الكف عنه والعزم على الترك) فالخير بالذات في حق المكلف المانع عن توجه العقاب هو عدم الحرام الذي هو الشر بالذات في حقه، لكن لما كان الكف وسيلة إلى إبقائه أمر المكلف به ومن ها هنا اندفع أنه لو كان المطلوب بالذات في النهي هو الكف لكان الحد مرتباً على عدمه لا على فعل الحرام، إذ ليس في النهي إلا مطلوب ،واحد وقد قلتم إنه الكف، وذلك لأن الشرية كانت بالذات في الحرام، وهو الموجب للعقاب في الآخرة بالنار وفي الدنيا بإقامة الحد، فالخير بالذات عدمه، وإنما طلب الكف لأنه وسيلة إليه ومانع عنه (وهو) أي كون الوسيلة التي هي الكف مقدورة (معنى مقدورية العدم و) هو أيضاً معنى أن أثرها) أي القدرة (الاستمرار فإن باستمرار الوسيلة يستمر العدم (وإلا) أي وإن لم يكن المعنى ما ذكر فلا لأن العدم من الأزل بانتفاء علة الوجود يصح، فالعدم أصلي، واستمراره باستمرار عدم علة الوجود لا بالقدرة إذ ما تحقق بعلة لا يتحقق بأخرى، فاندفع ما أورد على الاستدلال على عدم مقدورية العدم بأن العدم أزلي وثابت قبل القدرة، فلا يكون أثراً لها، فإنه يجوز أن يكون استمراره وبقاؤه أثراً للقدرة، وجه الدفع ظاهر، فإن البقاء إنما يكون ببقاء العلة، فبقاء العدم إنما يكون ببقاء عدم علة الوجود، فلا دخل للقدرة فيه فتعرّف (ولهذا) أي لأجل أن العدم لا يكون إلا بانتفاء مشيئة الوجود، والمشيئة إنما تتعلق بالكف (عرفوها بإن شاء فعل وإن شاء (ترك ففرّعوا الترك الذي هو الفعل على المشيئة (دون) أن يقولوا إن شاء لم يفعل) فلم يفرعوا العدم على المشيئة (أو) عرفوا بإن شاء فعل (وإن لم يشأ لم يفعل ففرعوا العدم على عدم المشيئة، هذا (قيل) إذا كان الكف واجباً ومكلفاً به فحين الغفلة عن المنهي عنه ( يلزم ترك الواجب وهو الكف فيعاقب) مراراً بترك هذا الواجب
Issue: There is no obligation except upon an act, contrary to many Mu'tazila who say that obligation attaches to non-existence as well. (It) means the act in prohibition is refraining of the self. Since the dispute revolves around whether non-existence is suitable for the attachment of obligation or not, and its basis is whether non-existence is within power or not, he intended to clarify this meaning so that the issue is completely uncovered. He said: There is no dispute about non-existence of an act due to absence of will, for the cause of non-existence is the absence of the cause of existence, and will is among the causes of existence; but this non-existence is not suitable as a locus for obligation and reward. Rather, the dispute is about the non-existence of the act by the will attached to it: does it exist in reality with this description or not? And it is this non-existence through which compliance in prohibition is realized and reward is attached, if it is realized. We say: The will does not attach to it, i.e., to non-existence essentially, so the non-existence arising from will is not realized in reality, because will requires thing-ness, and non-existence as such is pure nothing; therefore will does not attach to it. Therefore there is no way to it (i.e., non-existence) except by its (will's) attachment to what is a means to it, which is refraining from it and resolving to abandon. So the good in itself for the obligated person that prevents punishment is the non-existence of the unlawful, which is evil in itself for him. But since refraining is a means to its preservation, the obligated was commanded with it. And from here it is repelled that if the intended in itself in prohibition were refraining, then the penalty would be attached to its non-existence, not to the act of the unlawful, for in prohibition there is only one intended matter, and you said it is refraining. That is because evil-ness was in the unlawful itself, which necessitates punishment in the afterlife by fire and in this world by establishing the penalty. So the good in itself is its non-existence, and refraining is demanded only because it is a means to it and a preventer from it. (And it is) the fact that the means which is refraining is within power, which is the meaning of the power over non-existence, and it is also the meaning that its effect (i.e., of power) is continuation: by the continuation of the means, non-existence continues. Otherwise (i.e., if the meaning is not as mentioned), then it is not, because non-existence from eternity by the negation of the cause of existence is correct; so non-existence is original, and its continuation by continuation of the negation of the cause of existence, not by power, since what is realized by a cause cannot be realized by another. So what was objected to the proof of non-existence being within power—that non-existence is eternal and established before power, so it cannot be an effect of it—is repelled. For it is possible that its continuance and persistence be an effect of power. But the repelling point is apparent: persistence is only by persistence of the cause; persistence of non-existence is only by persistence of the negation of the cause of existence, so power has no role in it. Therefore, for this reason (i.e., because non-existence only occurs by negation of the will for existence, and will only attaches to refraining) they defined it as: 'if He wills, He does; if He wills, He leaves', so they derived leaving—which is an act—from will, instead of saying 'if He wills, He does not do'. Thus they did not derive non-existence from will. Or they defined it as: 'if He wills, He does; and if He does not will, He does not do', so they derived non-existence from the absence of will. It is said: if refraining is obligatory and commanded, then when one is heedless of the prohibited thing, it entails abandoning the obligatory—which is refraining—so he would be punished repeatedly for abandoning this obligation.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a usul rule discussing the principle that obligation (taklif) can only attach to acts (af'al), not to non-existence (adam). It begins by stating the Hanafi position against the Mu'tazila who claim that non-existence can also be the object of command. The key point: in a prohibition (nahy), what is commanded is the act of refraining (kaff), which is a real act of the self, not mere non-existence. The argument is that will (mashiyyah) only attaches to things that have being (shay'iyyah); non-existence is nothing, so cannot be directly willed or commanded. However, the command to refrain is a means to achieve the non-existence of the prohibited act. So the real good is the absence of the evil act, but the command is directed at the act of refraining. The text then addresses a subtle point about power (qudrah): non-existence itself is not within power because it is eternal and pre-dates power; what is within power is the continuation of non-existence through the continuation of the means (refraining). This refutes the claim that non-existence can be directly caused by power. Finally, it mentions a definition of power: 'if He wills, He does; if He wills, He leaves'—deriving leaving, which is an act, from will, not directly from non-existence. The last sentence raises a possible problem: if refraining is obligatory, then being heedless would mean abandoning the obligation, leading to repeated punishment. This is probably the beginning of an objection, but the text cuts off. The teacher should explain the Hanafi insistence that all commands and prohibitions ultimately relate to acts, not to absence of acts, and how this affects the understanding of sin and punishment.

Key Terms
الكف (al-kaff): The act of refraining or withholding oneself from the prohibited act.
العدم (al-‘adam): Non-existence; the absence of something. In usul, it is not a proper object of command.
المشيئة (al-mashiyyah): Divine will; in this context, it only attaches to things (act or object) that have reality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why, according to the Hanafi argument, can non-existence (al-‘adam) not be directly commanded?
A) Because non-existence is impossible to obey.
B) Because will (mashiyyah) can only attach to things that have 'thing-ness' (shay'iyyah).
C) Because non-existence is always caused by something else.
D) Because the Quran does not mention non-existence.

Key Takeaway
Obligation (taklif) attaches only to acts; in prohibitions, the commanded act is the act of refraining (kaff), not the non-existence of the prohibited act.

Definition of Compliance (Imtithal) and the Condition of Capability
Defining imtithal and refuting Mu'tazila on praise

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of compliance (imtithal) and apply the condition of capability (maqdur) to distinguish between active refraining and mere non-existence in prohibitions.

Core Idea
Compliance requires capability: only deliberate acts or refraining, not mere absence, earn reward.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut defines the core Hanafi concept of compliance (imtithal). The author clarifies that compliance which yields reward must be 'within capability' (maqdur): for commands, it is performing the act; for prohibitions, it is active refraining (kuff) — not merely the absence of the prohibited act. This distinction is critical when evaluating a person's legal responsibility and praiseworthiness, especially in refuting the Mu'tazila who claim that one who never even thinks of sinning is praised for the non-existence of the sin. We will unpack the definition, its conditions, and the Hanafi proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of imtithal
Find the passage where the author states that compliance which has reward is only through an act within capability. Note that in commands it is the act itself, in prohibitions it is refraining (kuff).
The key phrase: 'الامتثال الذي يترتب عليه الثواب لا يكون إلا بالمقدور'.
2
Distinguish active refraining from mere non-existence
Understand that the Hanafi position treats refraining (kuff) as a deliberate act of the will, not mere absence. This is crucial because punishment or praise attaches only to intentional acts within one's power.
Kuff is a fi'l, not just 'adam.
3
Analyze the case of the heedless (ghafla)
The passage discusses that at the time of heedlessness, there is no obligation. Once aware, determination becomes obligatory. If a person was capable but did not act, he is negligent (muqassir). Apply this to the scenario of adultery to see why mere non-existence is not praiseworthy.
The example: a man aware of adultery who does not commit it but does not actively refrain is not a sinner because the non-existence is already there, but he is not praised either.
4
Examine the Mu'tazila objection and Hanafi response
The Mu'tazila cite Quran 79:40-41 to argue that praise is for the non-existence of sin. The Hanafi response argues that the verse praises 'restraining the soul', which is active refraining. See how the Hanafi uses the same proof but interprets it differently.
The key term in the verse: 'نَهَى النَّفْسَ' implies active restraint.
5
Derive the usul principle
From this analysis, derive the principle: Obligation (taklif) presupposes capability. Compliance is only valid through a maqdur act. This principle applies across all fiqh chapters.
This is a foundational usul rule.

Source Text

المقالة الثانية في الأحكام

الامتثال)
قلنا : لا تكليف للغافل فحين الغفلة غير مكلف به فلا وجوب فلا عقاب (وبعد الشعور يجب العزم وإلا يعاقب على تركه بناء على عدم المقدور الواجب، وفيه أنه يلزم أن يكون الرجل الشاعر للزنا إذا لم يكف عنه ولم يفعل عاصياً، والإنصاف الديني يحكم بخلافه، إلا أن يلتزم ويقال : هذا العصيان مرفوع ، كما في الخبر الصحيح أن الهم بالسيئة لا يكتب، والحق أن الجواب المذكور تنزلي والحق في الجواب أن الكف إنما وجب لحصول حكمة عدم المنهي وحين الغفلة إذ قد تحقق عدم الحرام بنفسه سقط الوسيلة من غير عصيان لانتفاء سبب الوجوب، هذا (والحاصل أي حاصل البحث أن الامتثال الذي يترتب عليه الثواب (لا يكون إلا بالمقدور أي بالفعل المقدور (وهو الفعل في الأمر والكف في النهي، وأما عدم الموجب للعصيان (فيكون) تارة (بعدم المقدور كما في ترك الواجب فإن عدم المقدور يستمر لعدم تعلق القدرة، وقد كان قادراً على تعليقها، فيكون مقصراً (و) يكون عدم الامتثال تارة (بفعل المقدور أيضاً إذا كان المقدور شراً وعدمه خيراً كما في فعل الحرام) وذلك لأنه كسب بالقدرة شراً فيكون مقصراً (وأما العدم المقدور بالذات الذي يترتب عليه العقاب (فلعدمه) أي لكونه معدوماً غير متحقق لا دخل له في شيء من الثواب والعقاب، وإذا تمهد هذا (فلا يرد ما قيل لو لم يكن عدم الفعل مقدوراً لم يترتب الإثم في ترك الواجب إلا بالكف عنه) والتالي باطل والملازمة لأن المؤاخذة بما ليس في قدرته باطل، وأشار إلى وجه الدفع بقوله : (لأن الملازمة ممنوعة فإن الإثم قد يكون بعدم المقدور إذا كان واجباً، وفي ترك الواجب قد عدم الواجب المقدور (وإن لم يكن العدم في نفسه (مقدوراً) المعتزلة (قالوا : من دعي إلى زنا فلم يفعل يمدح على عدم الفعل بقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَأَمَّا مَنْ خَافَ مَقَامَ رَبِّهِ، وَنَهَى النَّفْسَ عَنِ الهَوَى فَإِنَّ الْجَنَّةَ هِيَ الْمَأْوَى ) [النازعات: 40-41] (من غير أن يخطر بباله فعل الضد) حتى ينسب المدح إليه قلنا : ممنوع أنه يمدح على عدم الفعل (بل) يمدح (للكف عنه هذا) وهو ظاهر.
The second article on rulings.

Compliance:
We said: There is no obligation for the heedless; at the time of heedlessness he is not obligated, so no obligation, so no punishment. And after becoming aware, determination is obligatory, otherwise he is punished for leaving it based on the non-existence of the obligatory that is within capability. In this there is that a man aware of adultery, if he does not refrain and does not commit it, would be a sinner. Religious fairness judges otherwise, unless he commits and it is said: this sin is lifted, as in the authentic hadith that the intention to do evil is not recorded. The truth is that the mentioned answer is metaphorical. And the correct answer is that refraining is only obligatory for the attainment of the wisdom of not doing the prohibited, and at the time of heedlessness, since the non-existence of the prohibited is already realized, the means falls away without sin due to the non-existence of the cause of obligation. This is the summary: that compliance upon which reward follows is only through the capable, i.e., an act within capability; it is the act in the case of a command and refraining in the case of a prohibition. As for the non-existence that necessitates sin, it is sometimes by non-existence of the capable, as in leaving an obligatory act, for the non-existence of the capable continues because power does not attach, and he was able to attach it, so he is negligent. And sometimes non-compliance is by doing the capable as well if the capable is evil and its non-existence is good, as in doing the prohibited, because he acquired evil through power, so he is negligent. As for the non-existence that is capable by itself which entails punishment, because it is non-existent, not realized, it has no part in reward or punishment. When this is established, then what is said does not apply: if the non-existence of the act were not capable, then sin in leaving an obligatory act would not be incurred except by refraining from it. The consequent is invalid, and the implication is invalid because holding someone accountable for what is not in his power is invalid. He indicated the rebuttal by his saying: The implication is denied, for sin may be by non-existence of the capable when it is obligatory, and in leaving the obligatory, the obligatory capable has been missed even if the non-existence itself is not capable. The Mu'tazila said: One who is invited to adultery and does not do it is praised for the non-existence of the act by His saying: "But as for he who feared the standing of his Lord and restrained his soul from desire, indeed Paradise will be his refuge" [79:40-41] without any thought of the opposite act occurring to his mind such that praise is attributed to him. We said: It is denied that he is praised for the non-existence of the act; rather he is praised for refraining from it. This is apparent.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a definition and analysis of the concept of compliance (imtithal) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author, commenting on the matn of Muslim al-Thubut, explains that compliance which leads to reward is only through an act that is within one's capability (maqdur). In a command, it is performing the act; in a prohibition, it is refraining. However, refraining is not simply the absence of action but an active choice to withhold. The heedless person is not obligated at the moment of heedlessness. Once aware, he must have the determination to act or refrain. The Mu'tazila object that a person who avoids adultery without even thinking about it is praised in the Quran, so praise is for non-existence of the act. The Hanafi response distinguishes between mere non-existence (which is not praiseworthy) and active refraining (kuff), which is itself an act of the will and thus within capability. Therefore, the praised act is refraining, not absence. This is a rational argument (dalil aqli) supported by Quranic proof.

Key Terms
الامتثال (al-imitithāl): Compliance: performing the commanded act or refraining from the prohibited act as required, with the intention of obedience, and it must be within one's capability.
المقدور (al-maqdūr): That which is within one's power or capability; the act that the mukallaf can choose to do or not do.
الكف (al-kaff): Active refraining; the deliberate choice to withhold from an act, which is within one's capability and thus a valid act of compliance in prohibitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is a person praised when invited to adultery but does not commit it?
A) Because he did not commit the sin, which is non-existence of the act.
B) Because he actively refrained from it, which is an act within his capability.
C) Because he had no intention to commit it from the start.
D) Because the sin was impossible for him to commit.

Key Takeaway
Compliance (imtithal) requires a deliberate act within capability; for prohibitions, this act is active refraining (kuff), not mere non-existence.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

The Hanafi Critique of Ash'ari's Denial of Taklif Before the Act
Refuting the attribution to Ash'ari and disputing continuance of taklif during the act

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that taklif must precede the act and evaluate the Ash'ari counter-argument about power with the act.

Core Idea
Obligation before the act is logically necessary; demanding the already existent is absurd.

This passage clarifies a common misattribution to Imam al-Ash'ari and then engages in a detailed dialectical critique of the position that taklif continues during the act. The Hanafi argument rests on the principle that demanding what already exists is impossible, and it critiques the Ash'ari notion of power accompanying the act. By the end, you'll understand why the Hanafi school insists on taklif before the act and why the alternative leads to logical and legal absurdities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the attributed position
What exactly is attributed to Ash'ari? The passage states he denied taklif before the act. But note: the text says this attribution is not textually proven.
2
Recognize the Hanafi refutation
The author shows the absurd consequences: no obligation on disbelievers, sinners not obligated, impossibility of compliance and intention.
3
Narrow the real dispute
The text clarifies that the dispute is about the continuance of taklif during the act, not its existence before. Ash'ari claimed it continues, Hanafi says it ends at the moment of act.
4
Work through the dialectical arguments
Follow the back-and-forth: Ash'ari says power with act, so act is within power; Hanafi replies power has no effect in their view; even if it does, the act is necessitated by choice; even if that is accepted, demanding the existent remains a barrier.
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
The correct view is that taklif is before the act, and it ceases upon occurrence. The passage also addresses the analysis of extended acts (mutamad) and the parts of demand, showing that demand precedes each part.

نسب إلى الأشعري أن لا تكليف قبل (الفعل وفيه إشارة إلى أن هذا لم يثبت عنه نصاً، ولعلهم أخذوا من قوله : القدرة مع الفعل لأن الشرط مع المشروط، وفيه ما فيه (وهو) أي هذا القول المنسوب إليه (غلط) بالضرورة ، كيف لا يكون غلطاً (و) حينئذ (يلزم نفي تكليف الكافر بالإيمان إذ الإيمان لم يوجد وقبله لا تكليف، بل لا يكون العاصي مكلفاً أصلاً، ولا سخافة فوق هذا (و) يلزم أيضاً (نفي الامتثال فإنه الإتيان كما كلف وهو إنما يكون (باختيار الفعل بعد العلم بالتكليف ولا يعلم التكليف أبداً قبل الفعل وأيضاً لا تصح نية أداء الواجب، فإن وجوبه لم يعلم بعد (ومع ذلك الفساد قد تبعه جماعة ، منهم صاحب المنهاج، والله در الإمام حيث قال : ( هذا مذهب لا يرتضيه عاقل لنفسه أن يقول : هذا مذهبي (و) قال (في الأحكام) في تقرير النزاع»، التكليف ثابت (قبله أي الفعل البتة لا ينكره الأشعري (ومنقطع) بعده أيضاً البتة اتفاقاً و إنما النزاع في بقائه حال الفعل هل هو باق حال حدوثه؟ قال به

الأشعري وأبطل بأنه تكليف بإيجاد الموجود، ورد بأن إيجاد الموجود بهذا الإيجاد غير ممتنع والمصنف قرر بنمط آخر وقال : (وهو باطل، لأنه كما تقول الطلب باق حين وجود المطلوب، وهو) أي طلب الموجود باطل بالضرورة كما ترى وقد يؤوّل بأن المراد بالتكليف إيقاع المكلف في الكلفة، ولا شك في بقائه، وحينئذ لا يرد شيء، والقول بأنه لم يقل ببقاء الطلب بل ببقاء اشتغال الذمة غير تام فإن اشتغال الذمة بالأمر المتحقق مما لا يعقل فافهم (وما يقال) لتصحيحه (إن التكليف متعلق بالمجموع من الفعل من حيث المجموع (وهو يحدث شيئاً فشيئاً) على التدريج (فيلزم مقارنته بالحدوث ولا يلزم طلب الموجود، لأنه إنما يوجد إذا وجد الجزء الأخير فمع أنه لا يتم في (الآنيات إذ ليس حدوثها شيئاً فشيئاً (فاسد، لأن الفعل إذا كان ممتداً كان الطلب المتعلق به محللاً إلى الأجزاء حسب أجزاء الفعل، وكل جزء من الفعل تعلق به جزء من الطلب فكل جزء منه مسبوق بجزء من الطلب المتعلق به وهذا ظاهر، فإن قلت : المطلوب بالذات ليس إلا المجموع بما هو المجموع، وإن كان الطلب المتعلق به ذا أجزاء بالعرض والطلب المتعلق بالمجموع متحقق حال ابتداء حدوثه فتم مطلوب الخصم قلت : إن طلب المجموع بما هو مجموع موجود قبل حدوثه، فإن حدوثه ليس في أول الأجزاء، إذ لم يوجد بعض أجزائه بعد، وكذا طلب كل جزء قبله، فلا معية أصلاً فتأمل، وتشكر الأشعرية (قالوا : الفعل مقدور حينئذ أي حين وجوده (لأنه أثر القدرة) وأثرها مقدور، وإذا كان مقدوراً (فيصح التكليف (به في هذا الحين إذ لا مانع من التكليف إلا عدم القدرة، وقد انتفى أيضاً قلنا: لا نسلم أنه أثرها فإنه لا تأثير للقدرة عندكم) أصلاً، لا في الكسب ولا في الإيجاد، ولما كان هذا الجواب جدلياً وفاسداً أيضاً لأنه أراد بأثر القدرة ما تعلقت به القدرة المتوهمة التي هي مدار صحة التكليف عنده لم يكتف به، وأجاب بعد تسليمه وقال (ولو سلم أنه أثر القدرة كما هو مذهبنا إذ لها دخل وتأثير في الكسب (فلا نسلم أنه يستلزم المقدورية، فإنه يجب الفعل بالاختيار، لأن الشيء ما لم يجب لم يوجد) والواجب لا يكون مقدوراً، ولما كان هذا أيضاً فاسداً لا لأنهم يجوزون الوجود من غير وجوب، وترجيح المختار أحد المتساويين، ولهذا صححوا حدوث العالم مع كونه مستنداً إلى الباري عز وجل، فإنك قد عرفت أن الوجود من غير وجوب باطل، وكذا الترجيح من غير رجحان وتصحيح الحدوث لا مقدور (فلا نسلم أن لا مانع إلا ذلك، بل لزوم طلب الموجود أيضاً مانع .
Issue:
It is attributed to al-Ash'ari that there is no obligation before the act. In this there is an indication that this is not established from him textually. Perhaps they took it from his statement: Power is with the act, because the condition is with the conditioned. There is something in it. And this statement attributed to him is necessarily false. How could it not be false? Then it would entail the negation of obligation upon the disbeliever to believe, since belief does not exist and before it there is no obligation. Rather the sinner would not be obligated at all, and there is no absurdity beyond this. Also it entails negation of compliance, for compliance is performing as commanded, and that only occurs by choosing the act after knowledge of obligation, and he never knows the obligation before the act. Also the intention to perform an obligatory act would not be valid, since its obligation is not known yet. Despite this corruption, a group followed him, including the author of al-Minhaj. May Allah reward the Imam who said: This is a madhhab that no intelligent person would approve for himself to say: this is my madhhab. And he said in al-Ahkam concerning the formulation of the dispute: Obligation is established before the act absolutely; al-Ash'ari does not deny that. And it is cut off after the act absolutely by agreement. The dispute is only about its continuance during the act: is it remaining at the moment of its occurrence? Al-Ash'ari said yes. And it is invalidated as being an obligation to bring into existence what already exists. It is replied that bringing into existence what already exists by this act of bringing is not impossible. The author stated in another manner and said: It is false because, as you would say, the demand remains when the demanded is present, and demanding the existent is necessarily false as you see. It may be interpreted that by taklif is meant the falling of the mukallaf into difficulty (kulfa), and there is no doubt of its continuance, then nothing applies. The statement that he did not say the demand remains but rather the engagement of the dhimmah remains is incomplete, for engagement of the dhimmah with something actual is not rational. So understand. And what is said to correct it: that obligation attaches to the whole of the act as a whole, and it occurs bit by bit gradually, so it entails its accompaniment with occurrence and does not entail demanding the existent, because it only exists when the last part exists. But this is not the case for instantaneous acts (al-aniyat) since their occurrence is not bit by bit. It is false because if the act is extended, the demand attached to it is analyzed into parts according to the parts of the act, and each part of the act has a part of the demand attached to it, so each part is preceded by a part of the demand attached to it, and this is apparent. If you say: The intended demanded is only the whole as a whole, even if the demand attached to it has parts accidentally, and the demand attached to the whole is realized at the start of its occurrence, then the opponent's objective is achieved. I say: The demand of the whole as a whole exists before its occurrence, for its occurrence is not at the first of the parts since some of its parts have not yet existed. Likewise the demand for each part is before it, so there is no companionship at all. So reflect. And the Ash'ariyya said: The act is within power at that moment, i.e., at its occurrence, because it is the effect of power, and its effect is within power. If it is within power, then obligation is valid at that moment, since there is no prevention from obligation except lack of power, and that is removed. We said: We do not accept that it is its effect, for power has no effect according to you at all, neither in acquisition (kasb) nor in bringing into existence. Since this answer was dialectical and also false because he meant by effect of power that which the supposed power attaches to, which is the basis of validity of obligation according to him, he was not satisfied with it. And he answered after accepting it and said: Even if we accept that it is the effect of power as is our madhhab, since it has influence in acquisition, we do not accept that it entails being within power, for the act is necessitated by choice, for a thing is not brought into existence unless it is necessitated, and the necessitated is not within power. Since this also is false, not because they allow existence without necessity and preponderance of equal alternatives, and for this they affirmed the occurrence of the world despite its being dependent on the Creator, for you have known that existence without necessity is false, likewise preponderance without preference. And affirming occurrence does not depend on this; rather it is valid with necessity as we indicated earlier. Rather because necessity by choice does not entail compulsion nor lack of power as we explained earlier. He was not satisfied with this answer either and answered with another face and said: Even if we accept that the effect of power is within power, we do not accept that there is no prevention except that; rather the necessity of demanding the existent is also a prevention.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage addresses a position attributed to al-Ash'ari denying taklif (obligation) before the act. The author refutes it as necessarily false, as it would negate obligation on disbelievers and sinners before they act, leading to absurdities. The real dispute is about the continuance of taklif at the moment of the act. Ash'ari holds that the obligation remains during the act, while the Hanafis argue it would entail demanding the already existent, which is invalid. The passage includes a detailed dialectic: Ash'ari respond that power is with the act, so the act is within power at the moment of occurrence. The Hanafi response denies that power has any effect (on the Ash'ari view) and then even if accepted, argues that the act is necessitated by choice and thus not within power. Further arguments involve the analysis of extended acts and the parts of demand. The author concludes that the best answer is that requiring the existent is still a prevention. This is a critical refinement of the matn's position.

Key Terms
التكليف (al-taklīf): The imposition of a legal obligation (command or prohibition) by the Lawgiver upon a capable subject.
القدرة (al-qudra): Power or ability to perform an act; a condition for the validity of taklif.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response, why is it invalid for taklif to continue during the act?
A) Because power is only available before the act.
B) Because it would require demanding the already existent act.
C) Because the act is impossible to perform.
D) Because the mukallaf is no longer capable.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that taklif must precede the act and does not continue during it, avoiding the logical absurdity of demanding what already exists.

Power as a Condition of Obligation: Hanafi Timing
Stating the agreement on qudra as a condition and the Hanafi view on its timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the timing of qudra as a condition of taklif and distinguish it from the Ash'ari view.

Core Idea
Power must precede the act for obligation to be valid — this is the Hanafi position.

In this passage, the author states an agreed-upon principle: that power (qudra) is a condition for taklif. However, the Hanafi school uniquely holds that this power must exist before the act, not simultaneously. This lesson explores the implications of this timing issue for understanding how obligations are imposed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed-upon premise
The passage first states that power is a condition for taklif by agreement among Ahl al-Sunna. Recognize this as a foundational usul principle.
2
Locate the Hanafi specificity
The text then adds 'but this power exists before the act according to us (Hanafis)'. This specifies the Hanafi view on timing.
The wording 'عندنا' indicates the school's position.
3
Understand the opposing view
The passage hints at disagreement: others differ on the modality. The Ash'ari view holds that power is simultaneous with the act. Understand this contrast.
This is a key point of ikhtilaf between Hanafi and Ash'ari usul.
4
Appreciate the consequence
The timing of qudra affects whether an obligation can be imposed on someone who becomes capable only at the moment of the act. The Hanafi view ensures that the mukallaf is already capable when commanded.
This has practical fiqh implications, e.g., in fasting, Hajj, etc.

مسألة
(القدرة شرط التكليف اتفاقاً بين أهل السنة القامعين للبدعة، وأكثر أهل الأهواء أيضاً وافقنا، وإن خالفونا في كيفية تأثير القدرة (لكن) هذه القدرة موجودة (قبل الفعل عندنا) معشر
Issue:
Power is a condition of obligation by agreement among the Ahl al-Sunna who suppress innovation, and most of the people of desires also agreed with us, even if they disagree with us about the modality of power's effect. But this power exists before the act according to us, the community (of Hanafis).
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This is a brief matn-style statement establishing a fundamental principle: power (qudra) is a necessary condition for the validity of taklif (obligation). This is agreed upon by Ahl al-Sunna and even most deviant sects, though they differ on how power operates. The Hanafi position is that this power must exist before the act. This contrasts with the Ash'ari view that power is simultaneous with the act. The passage is incomplete in this window, but the core point is clear: Hanafis affirm pre-act capability.

Key Terms
القدرة (al-qudra): The ability of the mukallaf to perform an act, a condition for the validity of obligation.
شرط التكليف (sharṭ al-taklīf): A condition without which the obligation is not valid or not applicable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Simultaneous with the act.
B) After the act.
C) Before the act.
D) It is not specified.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires power (qudra) to exist before the act for obligation to be valid.

Does Qudra Precede the Act? The Hanafi-Ash'ari Dispute
Rational argument for prior qudra

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on qudra as a condition for taklif and evaluate the Ash'ari counter-argument using rational proofs.

Core Idea
Qudra must be before the act; without prior capacity, obligation is invalid.

A key debate in usul al-fiqh is whether capacity (qudra) must exist before the obligated act or simultaneously. The Hanafi Maturidi school insists on priority, while the Ash'aris accept simultaneity. Understanding this difference is crucial for theories of obligation and responsibility. This lesson unpacks the rational arguments and their practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Contested Issue
Recognize that the dispute is about the timing of qudra relative to the act: does it precede or coincide?
2
State the Hanafi Position
The Hanafis hold that qudra is a condition (shart) of taklif and must exist before the conditioned act.
Use the text: 'لنا أولاً: أنها شرط الفعل اختياراً، وهو قبل المشروط'
3
Analyze the First Proof (Analogy of Condition)
Understand the argument that a condition naturally precedes its conditioned, though this may be logical priority, not necessarily temporal.
The text notes a subtlety about natural vs. temporal priority.
4
Analyze the Second Proof (Example of the Disbeliever)
If qudra were simultaneous, the disbeliever would not be obligated for faith before the act, but he is obligated, so qudra must precede.
This shows the impossibility of taklif without prior capacity.
5
Understand the Ash'ari Response and Hanafi Rebuttal
The Ash'aris argue that it suffices that the opposite of the act is possible. The Hanafi rebuttal: this fails when the agent is incapable of both act and opposite.
The text concludes that the disagreement only arises when the agent has an alternative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقالة الثانية في الأحكام الماتريدية (وعند المعتزلة (و) موجودة (معه) لا قبله عند الأشعرية لنا أولاً: أنها شرط الفعل اختياراً، وهو قبل المشروط تدبر فإنه لقائل أن يقول : إن تقدم الشرط على المشروط إنما هو تقدم بالطبع، ولا يجب بحسب الزمان وكان الكلام فيه وفيه غلط باشتراك الاسم، ولعل هذا مشي على ما قاله المتكلمون إن وجود المعلول من الفاعل المختار يكون بعد وجود الاختيار بعدية زمانية، وأن المراد يجب تأخره صريحاً عن إرادة المريد، ولذا امتنعوا من أن يكون معلول المختار قديماً (و) لنا (ثانياً : لو كانت القدرة معه لزم عدم كون الكافر مكلفاً بالإيمان قبله، لأنه غير مقدور له في تلك الحالة ولا تكليف بغير المقدور، ولا تصغ إلى قول من يرى تكليف المحال واقعاً (وأجيب) من قبل الأشعرية (شرط) التكليف عندنا أن يكون هو) أي الفعل نفسه متعلق القدرة (أو يكون (ضده) متعلقاً لها، وها هنا الإيمان، وإن كان غير مقدور للكافر لكن ضده الذي هو الكفر مقدوره البتة، فيصح التكليف (كذا في المواقف) فإن قلت : فعلى هذا يكون تكليف العاجز واقعاً عندهم قاطبة، فلا يصح نسبة الخلاف فيما بينهم قلت : ما سبق هو ما كان المكلف عاجزاً عنه وعن ضده، فلا تنافي، فافهم
The second article on the rulings of the Maturidis: (And according to the Mu'tazila (and) it (power) exists with it (the act) not before it, according to the Ash'aris. For us (Hanafis) first: that it (power) is a condition for the act by choice, and it is before the conditioned. Reflect, for one can say: The priority of the condition over the conditioned is only natural priority, not necessarily temporal, and the discussion is about that and there is a confusion due to homonymy. And perhaps this follows what the theologians said: that the existence of the effect from the free agent is after the existence of choice in terms of temporal posteriority, and that what is intended must be explicitly posterior to the will of the willer, and so they prevented the effect of the free agent from being eternal. And for us (secondly): If power were with the act, it would necessitate that the disbeliever is not obligated for faith before the act, because it is not possible for him in that state, and there is no obligation for the impossible. And do not listen to the one who holds that obligation of the impossible occurs. (And it was answered) by the Ash'aris: The condition for obligation according to us is that the act itself is attached to power, or its opposite is attached to it. And here faith, even if it is not possible for the disbeliever, but its opposite, which is disbelief, is definitely possible for him, so the obligation is valid. (As in al-Mawaqif). Then if you say: On this, the obligation of the incapable would occur according to them universally, so the disagreement among them cannot be attributed, I say: What preceded is the case where the obligated is incapable of both the act and its opposite, so there is no contradiction. So understand.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage presents the Maturidi (Hanafi) position on the timing of qudra (capacity) as a condition for taklif. The Hanafi view is that qudra must exist before the act, not simultaneously. They give two arguments: first, by analogy to a condition generally preceding the conditioned; second, by the example of the disbeliever: if qudra only existed at the time of the act, the disbeliever would not be obligated for faith before that moment, which contradicts the clear obligation of faith. The Ash'ari response is that it is sufficient that the opposite of the act (disbelief) is possible for the disbeliever, even if faith itself is not. The Hanafi author rebuts this by noting that if the person is incapable of both, then there is an issue. The lesson underscores the importance of capacity preceding the obligation.

Key Terms
قدرة (qudra): Capacity or power to perform an act; a condition for the validity of taklif.
تكليف (taklif): Legal obligation; the imposition of a duty on a legally responsible person.
شرط (shart): Condition; something whose presence is necessary for the validity of another thing but is not part of it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented in the passage, why would simultaneous qudra be problematic for the obligation of the disbeliever?
A) The disbeliever would be obligated for faith without prior capacity to believe.
B) The disbeliever would be obligated for faith only after believing.
C) Simultaneous qudra would make the act impossible.
D) The disbeliever has no capacity for disbelief.

Key Takeaway
For taklif to be valid, qudra (capacity) must exist before the act, not simultaneously with it, as argued by Hanafi Maturidis using rational proofs.
