Hanafi Division of Ability and Its Consequences for Obligation
Definition of qudra types and their legal effects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi division of qudra into mumkina and muyassara and apply the ruling on obligation and qada in the last part of time scenario.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, ability (qudra) is of two types: possible and facilitated; the latter allows obligation even when performance seems impossible, based on the possibility of time extension.

The Hanafi school classifies the ability required for obligation (taklif) into two categories: possible ability (al-qudra al-mumkina), which is the normal capacity through sound limbs and means, and facilitated ability (al-qudra al-muyassara), an additional divine favor that eases action. This distinction has practical consequences for when an act must be performed immediately and when qada is required. A key application is the scenario of the last part of the prayer time, where the act cannot normally be completed—here the Hanafis rule that obligation still rests, contrary to Zufar, relying on the possibility of divine extension of time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of qudra
Read the first part of the passage and list the two types: al-qudra al-mumkina (possible ability) and al-qudra al-muyassara (facilitated ability). Note how each is defined—mumkina by soundness of limbs and causes, muyassara by divine easing.
The author clarifies that the definition of mumkina is by necessary concomitant, not the essence of qudra.
2
Understand the function of the first ability in obligation and qada
The first ability is a condition for performing every wajib. The ruling on performance and qada depends on whether the act usually occurs with this ability and resolve. If yes, immediate performance is obligatory; if lost without negligence, qada is required only if the act has a substitute.
The text distinguishes between acts with a substitute (e.g., daily prayers) and those without (e.g., Eid prayer).
3
Apply to the last part of time scenario
Consider the case where a person has only the last part of time (al-juz' al-akhir) to perform an obligatory prayer, insufficient to complete it. According to the Hanafis, since the act does not usually occur with the first ability, immediate performance is not obligatory in kind; rather, the obligation is to establish the basis for qada. This means the person must still attempt the prayer, and if it is missed, qada is obligatory.
This is because the last part might extend through divine intervention, so the capacity is potentially present.
4
Compare with Zufar's position
Zufar denies obligation in this scenario, arguing that impossibility at the time negates obligation, analogous to carrying a mountain. The Hanafi response: the last part is not certainly the end due to possible extension, so the analogy fails.
The passage recounts historical miracles (sun stopping for Yusha' and Sulayman) to illustrate the possibility of time extension.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis require the person to pray in the last part and, if missed, perform qada; Zufar would say no prayer and no qada. This affects the ruling for someone who delays until the last moment.
The relied-upon view is the majority Hanafi position, as supported by al-Tahrir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة (قسم الحنفية القدرة (المشروطة في التكليف إلى ممكنة مفسرة بسلامة الآلات وصحة الأسباب، وهو تفسير باللازم فإن القدرة حقيقة صفة بها إن شاء فعل وإن لم يشأ لم يفعل، وهذه الصفة ملزومة لسلامة الآلات فإن عديم الرجل لا يقدر على القيام (وإلى ميسرة فاضلة عليها فضلاً منه تعالى باليسر) وهي صفة بها قدر الإنسان على الفعل صحة أسباب اليسر أيضاً (و) القدرة (الأولى) شرط في أداء كل واجب، لكن إن كان الفعل بها مع العزم غالباً) وقوعاً (فالواجب) على القادر (الأداء ) أي أداء الفعل الواجب المشروط بهذه القدرة فقط (عيناً) لا لأجل وجوب القضاء فإن فات الواجب منه (بلا تقصير لم يأثم ووجب القضاء إن كان له خلف وإلا يكن له خلف كالعيد (فلا قضاء) لعدمه (ولا إثم) لعدم التقصير (وإن قصر) وفوت الواجب (أثم مطلقاً) سواء كان له خلف ووجب القضاء أولا وإن لم يكن) الفعل بها مع العزم (غالباً) وقوعاً (وجب الأداء ) لا بعينه بل (ليترتب عليه (القضاء كالأهلية في الجزء الأخير من الوقت بحيث لا يسع الواجب (خلافاً لزفر) فإنه يقول: لا وجوب في هذه الصورة فلا قضاء لاعتباره قدر ما يحتمله الأداء حتى يعد المكلف قادراً عادة، كيف لا وأي فرق بين في هذا الجزء وبين حمل الجبل، فإنهما لا يتصوران منه بالقدرة الموجودة، وكلاهما ممكنان بالمتوهمة (و) قال في «التحرير») وإنما يجب عليه (لأنه لا قطع بالأخير) أي بكونه أخيراً لإمكان الامتداد بإيقاف الله تعالى الشمس، كما حكي عن يوشع على نبينا وآله وعليه الصلاة والسلام حين غزا الجبابرة يوم الجمعة وكادت الشمس تغرب فقال للشمس : قفي لا تدخل ليلة السبت، فلما فرغ عن القتال واستأصلهم ،غربت، وعن سليمان على نبينا وعليه الصلاة والسلام حين كادت صلاة العصر تفوته أقول يلزم عليه أن لا يقطع بالتضييق) لقيام احتمال الامتداد (وقد يقطع) وفيه أنه يلتزم عدم القطع وأي دليل على امتناعه (و) يلزم (أيضاً الامتداد إما بازدياد الأجزاء فيتسع الوقت حينئذ (ولا) نزاع فيه بل في التضييق (أو بالمد والبسط) أي بامتداد الجزء الأخير وانبساطه فيلزم بطلان القول بالجزء) لأنه قد امتد وانقسم، وفيه أن له أن يختار الشق الأول ويقول : إن المظنون أخيراً يمكن أن لا يبقى أخيراً لاحتمال امتداد وقته المقدر شرعاً بازدياد الأجزاء فيه كتخلل زمان الوقوف للشمس في زمان الحركة حتى الأداء (
Issue: The Hanafis divided ability (which is a condition for obligation) into (1) possible (mumkina), explained as soundness of limbs and correctness of causes—this is an interpretation by necessary concomitant, for ability in reality is a quality by which if one wills he acts and if he does not will he does not act, and this quality necessarily implies soundness of limbs; a person without a leg cannot stand. (2) Facilitated (muyassara), which is additional to it, a favor from Him Almighty by easing, and it is a quality by which a person is able to perform the act with soundness of the causes of ease also. The first ability is a condition for performing every obligation, but if the act with it (and with resolve) is usually occurring, then the obligation upon the capable person is performance (ada') in kind ('ayan), not for the sake of the obligation of qada'. If the obligatory act is lost from him without negligence, he does not sin, and qada' is obligatory if it has a substitute; if it has no substitute like the Eid prayer, then no qada' (due to its non-existence) and no sin (due to lack of negligence). If he is negligent and loses the obligation, he sins absolutely, whether it has a substitute and qada' is obligatory or not. And if the act with it (and with resolve) is not usually occurring, then performance is obligatory, not in kind but in order that qada' rests upon him, like eligibility (ahliyya) in the last part of time such that the obligatory act does not fit, contrary to Zufar. For he says: There is no obligation in this scenario, so no qada', because he considers the extent of what performance can bear so that the obligated person is considered capable customarily. How not? What difference is there between this part and carrying a mountain? Both are not conceivable from him with the existing ability, and both are possible through imaginative ability. And (the author) said in al-Tahrir: Rather, it is obligatory upon him because there is no certainty that it is the last (part), due to the possibility of extension by Allah stopping the sun, as narrated about Yusha' (peace be upon him) when he fought the giants on Friday and the sun was about to set; he said to the sun: 'Stop, do not enter the night of Saturday.' When he finished fighting and exterminated them, it set. And about Sulayman (peace be upon him) when the afternoon prayer was about to be missed. I say: It follows from this that he should not be certain of constraint due to the possibility of extension. (And it is sometimes certain.) There is the objection that he adheres to non-certainty, and what proof is there for its impossibility? Also, extension follows either by increase of parts, in which case the time expands—there is no dispute in that, but in constraint—or by stretching and expansion, i.e., the last part extends and expands, so the notion of a 'part' is invalid because it has extended and divided. In it, he may choose the first alternative and say: What is thought to be last may not remain last due to the possibility of the extension of its time as determined by law through increase of parts, like the insertion of the time of the sun's stopping in the time of motion, until performance.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a mas'ala (issue) dividing ability (qudra) relevant to taklif into two types: mumkina (possible) and muyassara (facilitated). The first is defined by the soundness of limbs and instruments; the author clarifies that this is a necessary concomitant, not the essence. The real qudra is a quality enabling action or non-action. The second is an additional divine favor (taysir) enabling the act with ease. The first ability is a condition for performing any wajib, but the ruling on obligation and qada depends on whether the act typically occurs with this ability and resolve. If it usually occurs, the obligation is immediate 'ada', and if missed without negligence, qada is required only if the act has a substitute (like missed prayer vs. Eid). If missed with negligence, sin is incurred regardless. If the act does not usually occur with that ability (like being in the last part of time for prayer), then the obligation is not immediate performance but rather that the obligation of qada rests upon the person, based on eligibility. This is against Zufar, who denies obligation in such a case. The author then debates the issue using the possibility of time extension through miraculous events (sun stopping for Yusha' and Sulayman). Zufar's view is that if an act is impossible at the time, there is no obligation. The Hanafi rebuttal argues that since the last moment is not certain, one must assume the possibility of extension, thus the obligation stands and qada applies if missed. The passage engages with logical arguments about the nature of time and divine intervention.

Key Terms
القدرة الممكنة (al-qudra al-mumkina): Ability defined by soundness of limbs and means; a condition for the obligation of immediate performance.
القدرة الميسرة (al-qudra al-muyassara): An additional ability granted by divine facilitation that enables ease in performing the act.
الجزء الأخير من الوقت (al-juz' al-akhir min al-waqt): The last part of the time for a prayer (or obligation) where the act cannot normally be completed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi division, what is the ruling on someone who misses a prayer due to time running out in the last part of time if they did not act negligently?
A) They sin and must perform qada.
B) They do not sin but must perform qada if the prayer has a substitute.
C) They neither sin nor perform qada.
D) They sin but do not perform qada.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi division of qudra and the possibility of time extension lead to the ruling that obligation remains even in the last part of time, and qada is required if missed.
